QATAR DIETARY GUIDELINES FOR MOTHER AND CHILD (0–5 YEARS) 

## **Acknowledgements** 

The Health Promotion Department in the Ministry of Public Health acknowledges the work of the Working Group whose recommendations informed the development of the first edition of the **Qatar Dietary Guidelines for Mother & Child (0-5 Years).** 

## **Members included:** 

- Health Promotion Department- Ministry of Public Health

- Qatar Foundation

- Weill Cornell Medicine-Qatar

- Al-Ahli Hospital 

**==> picture [102 x 143] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Foreword** 

The **Qatar Dietary Guidelines for Mother and Child (0–5 Years)Qatar Dietary and Child (0–5 Years)** have been developed based on our belief that the health and well-being of mothers and young children form the foundation for a thriving society. These guidelines provide clear, evidence-based recommendations aimed at improving the nutritional status and overall health of women before and during pregnancy, and after giving birth, as well as during the early years of the child’s life. The guidelines address key stages—starting from preconception, through pregnancy and lactation, and extending into infancy and early childhood. It underscores the importance of adopting a healthy lifestyle that promotes the well-being of both mother and child. Moreover, these guidelines serve as a vital resource for healthcare providers and families. 

The guidelines are divided into seven chapters that address various essential topics such as diet and lifestyle before pregnancy; during pregnancy; postpartum; breastfeeding; complementary feeding; nutrition for toddlers and preschoolers; and the importance of selecting healthy fats while reducing sugar and salt intake. Each chapter is designed to empower individuals with practical advice to foster healthy habits and make informed decisions. 

The Health Promotion Department at the Ministry of Public Health hopes that these guidelines will be used as a scientific resource and a tool for developing future policies, programs, and initiatives aimed at enhancing maternal and child health. 

## **Dr Salah Abdulla Alyafei** 

Director, Health Promotion Department Ministry of Public Health

## **Importance of Diet and Lifestyle During the First 1000 Days of a Child’s Life Including Pregnancy** 

Throughout your pregnancy, you will be experiencing many physiological and psychological changes, during which adequate nutrition is required for your health as well as that of your baby. ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� plays an important role in ensuring your child’s adequate development and overall health. Your diet and lifestyle during this period are therefore critical and deserve your utmost attention[ [1]] . 

This chapter addresses a few aspects related to your diet and lifestyle during pregnancy, such as adequate gestational weight gain (GWG), healthy eating, in addition to other factors of importance (vitamin/mineral supplementation, dietary and lifestyle management of pregnancyrelated complications, physical activity, oral health, mental health, eating disorders, emotional eating, and food safety). The last part of the chapter focuses on pregnant women who developed gestational diabetes, which is a form of diabetes that appears during pregnancy. 

Some of the recommendations presented in this chapter are based on pregnancy trimesters. As you may have learned from your physician, your nine months of pregnancy are divided into three �����������������������������������������������������������������������������������[st] trimester: 0-13 weeks; 2[nd] trimester: 14-26 weeks and 3[rd ] trimester: 27-40 weeks. 

**==> picture [151 x 152] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [82 x 95] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [36 x 53] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
02<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## **Weight Gain During Pregnancy** 

The amount of weight that you gain during your pregnancy, also termed gestational weight gain �������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [1]] . Mothers who gain excessive weight are at a higher risk of developing certain complications during their pregnancy, such as high blood pressure and high blood sugar. They may also deliver large (macrosomic) babies who may be at increased risk for obesity and chronic diseases later in life. On the other hand, mothers with very low GWG are more likely to have early delivery (preterm) and small ����������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [2]] . Not only does ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ Studies showed that gaining excessive weight during your pregnancy will increase the amount of weight you retain after pregnancy. This will increase your risk of obesity, type II diabetes, and cardiovascular diseases[[3]] . 

The amount of weight you should aim to gain during your pregnancy depends to a large extent on your weight status **before pregnancy** (i.e., whether you had a normal body mass index (BMI) before your pregnancy or whether you were underweight, overweight, or obese) (Refer to ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� of weight you should gain during your pregnancy will also depend on whether you are pregnant with only one baby (singleton pregnancy) or with twins (check tables 1 and 2, respectively). 

As such, the recommended amount of weight gain during pregnancy is the highest for women who were underweight before pregnancy (BMI <18.5 kg/m2). In contrast, the recommended amount of weight gain during pregnancy is the lowest for women who were obese before ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� throughout their pregnancy compared to women with a lower BMI. **It is important to note that weight loss is not recommended during pregnancy, unless medically indicated.** Instead, overweight and obese women are recommended **to lose the excess weight before getting pregnant (never during the pregnancy itself).** 

If you are pregnant with one baby (singleton pregnancy), refer to Table 1, which provides you with weight gain recommendations based on your pre-pregnancy BMI. If you are pregnant with twins, refer to Table 2. In all cases, make sure to consult a dietitian to help you plan for your weight gain and diet during pregnancy. 

**==> picture [89 x 77] intentionally omitted <==**

Table 1. Recommendations for Gestational Weight Gain (GWG) for a singleton pregnancy[ [4, 5]] 

|**Pre-pregnancy BMI category**|**Total weight gain**<br>**during pregnancy (kg)**|**Average rate of weight**<br>**gain during the 2nd**<br>**and 3rd trimesters in**<br>**g/week**|
|---|---|---|
|Underweight (<18.5 kg/m2)|12.5 - 18 kg|~ 510 g/week|
|Normal weight (18.5–24.9 kg/m2)|11.5 - 16 kg|~ 420 g/week|
|Overweight (25.0–29.9 kg/m2)|7 - 11.5 kg|~ 280 g/week|
|���������������2)|5 - 9 kg|~ 220 g/week|



Table 2. Recommendations for Gestational Weight Gain (GWG) for a twin pregnancy[[4, 5]] 

|**Pre-pregnancy BMI category**|**Total weight**<br>**gain during**<br>**pregnancy**|**Average rate**<br>**of weight gain**<br>**during the 2nd**<br>**trimester**|**Average rates**<br>**of weight gain**<br>**during the 3rd**<br>**trimester**|
|---|---|---|---|
|Underweight (<18.5 kg/m2)|�����������������������������������|||
|Normal weight (18.5–24.9 kg/m2)|16.8 - 24.5 kg|~ 770 g/week|~ 670 g/week|
|Overweight (25.0–29.9 kg/m2)|14.1 - 22.7 kg|~ 720 g/week|~ 610g/week|
|���������������2)|11.4 - 19.1 kg|~  450 g/week|~ 580 g/week|



If you are pregnant with triplets or other higher-order multiples, consult with your doctor and dietitian for advice on your weight gain. 

In all cases, it is important that you work closely with your dietitian to maintain your GWG within the recommended range.

## **Dietary Recommendations During Pregnancy** 

## 3.1. Consume a balanced and diverse diet 

The dietary intake recommendations for non-pregnant women are shown in Box 1.  The same �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� fact that you will need to take additional energy and protein as compared to when you were not pregnant (refer to section 3.3 for recommendations regarding your energy intake). 

Eating a variety of foods from the six food groups every day is the ideal way to provide all the essential nutrients to your body as well as to your baby. The six food groups include (Vegetables, Fruits, Cereals and starchy vegetables, Legumes, Milk, dairy products & alternatives, Fish, poultry, meat & alternatives). To achieve a healthy and balanced diet, it is also recommended that you limit your consumption of foods that are high in sugar, salt, and unhealthy fats such as commercially prepared foods and snacks. These foods are high in calories and hence will make you gain excessive weight. These foods are also unhealthy for your baby and can increase your baby’s risk for obesity and chronic disease later in life. It is important to note that many of the ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� manifested until later in the child’s life. 

Box 1 provides you with some general dietary recommendations[[6-12]] , **make sure to consult with your dietitian** ���������������������������������������������

## **Practical tips:** 

- Choose a wide variety and color of vegetables. 

- Eat vegetables with most meals, including snacks. 

- Favor fresh vegetables in season. 

- Choose vegetables prepared with little or no added salt, oil or fat. 

- Eat adequate amounts daily since vegetables help you feel full and are low in calories. 

- Cook side vegetables (broccoli, carrots, zucchini) by lightly steaming or stir-frying to preserve nutrients. 

- Eat more greens and leafy vegetables (fattouch, tabbouleh, green thyme, arugula, cabbage, or spinach salad). 

- In restaurants, order salad dressing separately and limit how much you add. 

- Eat raw vegetables as snacks with low-fat dip. 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- Eat more vegetable-based dishes such as saloona (traditional stew). 

- When eating out, choose plain vegetables instead of breaded or deep fried. 

- Avoid adding butter or margarine and rich sauces to vegetables. Use fresh or dried spices, herbs, or ��������������������� 

- Favor fresh vegetables over canned ones. When choosing canned vegetables, make sure to rinse them with water to lower the salt content. 

- Add a plate of fresh cut vegetables with your main meals.

Eat legumes daily. Legumes are rich in protein

Maintain a daily consumption of protein foods which include legumes, unsalted and raw nuts and seeds, �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� number of servings and serving sizes. 

## **Practical tips:** 

- Make legumes (lentils, beans, chickpeas) one of your main protein sources. 

- Choose legumes that are prepared with little or no added fats or oils. 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������

- Try vegetarian dishes from other cultures such as bean burritos and dahl. 

- Rinse canned beans with water before using to decrease salt content. 

- Include foods rich in vitamin C (tomatoes, peppers, lemon) with meals to enhance the absorption of iron and zinc from legumes. 

- Wait for at least one hour after meals before drinking tea to allow the absorption of iron from foods. 

- Cooking dry legumes instead of canned varieties is cheaper and decreases packaging waste, and exposure to chemicals from cans.

## **Poultry and meat: Choose skinless poultry and lean cuts of meat:** 

- Remove skin from poultry before cooking or buy skinless pieces. 

- Limit your consumption of red meat to no more than 500 g per week[[14]] . 

- Limit your consumption of processed luncheon and deli meats such as corned beef, hot dogs, sausages, pepperoni, salami, and smoked meat, as they are high in salt and nitrates (cancer-causing constituents). Make sandwiches with lower fat, unprocessed options such as roast beef, turkey, or chicken. 

- Choose less fatty cuts of meat such as leg of lamb (after removing visible fat), lean ground beef, and beef tenderloin. 

- Tenderize lean cuts of meat by using a marinade or a slow cooking method such as stewing or braising. 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- Broil, grill, roast, poach or boil poultry and meat instead of frying. 

- If frying meat, use little oil. 

- Prepare your foods without coating (such as breaded foods); avoid rich sauces and gravies. 

- Limit pre-prepared breaded foods such as nuggets. 

## **Eggs:** 

- Limit raw or partially cooked eggs or foods containing raw eggs. 

- Boiled eggs are nutritious and great to have for breakfast or dinner. 

## **Nuts and seeds:** 

- Aim for unsalted, raw nuts and seeds, rather than fried ones. 

- Choose unsalted, raw nuts and seeds, as part of a healthy snack and in moderate quantities (¼ cup). 

- Top your salad with unsalted, raw nuts or seeds. 

- Add some unsalted, raw nuts to your yogurt or oatmeal in the morning. 

“For more information on alternatives for animal-based protein foods, see Box 8. Dietary recommendations for vegetarian and vegan women.”

## 3.3. Energy intake during pregnancy 

## **���������������������������������������������������������������������������** 

����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� recommendations. In general, **���������������������������������������������������������������� trimester of your pregnancy.** 

In other words, if your usual energy intake was 1800 kcal per day before pregnancy, then you should �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

## **�����������������������������������������������������������** 

In general, you need to increase your energy intake by 340 kcal/ day in the second trimester and by 452 kcal/day in the third (Box 4). These recommendations apply to you if you have started your pregnancy with a normal body weight (i.e. BMI within the normal range)[ [5, 17]] . If you were overweight, obese or underweight at the start of your pregnancy, the recommendations shown in Box 4 may not apply to you. You will need to consult with your dietitian ��������������������������������������������������������� 

**==> picture [121 x 111] intentionally omitted <==**

Box 4. Energy requirements during pregnancy if you have started your pregnancy with a normal body weight 

If you are starting your pregnancy with a healthy weight, you do not need to increase your energy intake until the second and third trimesters. 

- **First trimester:** No need to increase your caloric intake. However, it is important that you choose nutritious foods to help support your baby’s growth and development. 

- **Second trimester:** You need to add 340 kcal to your daily energy intake. 

- **Third trimester:** You need to add 452 kcal to your daily energy intake. 

- **Twin pregnancies:** If you are pregnant with twins, you will need to add 600 kcal per day during the second and third trimesters 

As you may probably realize, there is no need to eat twice as much food to meet your caloric needs during pregnancy. You can meet your requirements by simply adding a healthy snack or a small meal. Examples of snacks/meals that could be added to your diet to meet the additional calorie needs are presented in Box 5. Snacks that contain some protein (such as unsalted, raw nuts, legumes, yogurt, cheese) are important for you since your protein needs increase a bit during the second and third trimesters of pregnancy.

## 3.4. Importance of hydration 

�������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ��������������������������������������������[[18]] . Dehydration may lead to constipation, headache and dizziness in the pregnant women and may lead to early labor and poor development of the ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� [19, 20]��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� water is critical in countries with hot and humid weather, such as that in the State of Qatar. You may want to watch out for early signs of dehydration, such as: 

- Feeling of thirst 

- Dark-colored urine 

- Tiredness 

- Dizziness 

- Dry mouth 

- Headache 

- Infrequent urination 

If you experience any of those symptoms, try to rest and drink water and other healthy beverages ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� �������������������������������������������������������������� * 1 cup = 250 mL 

## Box 6. Tips to meet your water needs 

- ��������������������������������������������� 

- Choose water more often than other types of beverages. 

- If you do not like water, add a wedge of lime or lemon or any other vegetable or fruit to enhance the taste. 

- Choose water as a beverage to drink with meals, especially when eating out. This will help reduce your caloric intake. 

- Carry a reusable water bottle everywhere you go. 

- Choose water instead of sugar-sweetened beverages to help maintain your weight and the health of your teeth. 

- Drink more water in hot weather and when physically active (before, during and after exercise). 

- Set reminders on your phone for drinking water or use a water drinking application on your smart phone.

## 3.5. Supplementation during pregnancy 

It is important for you to consume adequate amounts of all the essential vitamins and minerals in order to have a normal pregnancy with lower risk of complications. In addition, these nutrients are vital for your baby’s development and growth. 

Following a varied, balanced healthy diet during your pregnancy will most likely provide you with the needed vitamins and minerals. That said, there are a few vitamins and minerals that deserve special attention and for which you may need to take supplements. These include iron, folic acid, vitamin D and calcium. However, before taking any supplements, it is recommended that you �������������������������������������������� 

**==> picture [132 x 132] intentionally omitted <==**

**Iron:** 

You need more iron during pregnancy, to meet your own needs as well as those of your baby. In ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� will develop anemia, a condition that can result in health complications for you and your baby. �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� Adequate iron intake during pregnancy can reduce your risk of having a low-birth weight baby (i.e., a very small baby), while also reducing the risk of early birth (preterm) and infant mortality. ���������������������������������������������������������[ [21, 22]] . 

**The WHO recommends daily oral iron supplementation with 30-60 mg of iron for pregnant women**[[23]] . If you had anemia before getting pregnant, make sure to discuss this with your doctor as you may require higher doses of iron supplementation. 

In addition to supplementation, it is important to include iron-rich foods in your daily diet. Refer to Tables 3 and 4 for examples of animal-based iron-rich foods as well as plant-based foods that contain iron, respectively. It is important to note that iron from animal sources (heme-iron) is more easily absorbed by the body compared to iron from plant sources (non-heme iron).

## **Excellent sources of Iron:**

- Lamb 

- Shrimp 

## **Adequate Sources of Iron:** 

- Leg and thigh of chicken or turkey 

- Tuna (light) 

- Breast of chicken or turkey 

## Table 4. Plant based iron sources

- Large white beans, cooked

In order to maximize iron absorption from your foods, it is advisable to: 

- Add a source of vitamin C to your meal, such as tomatoes, peppers, broccoli, strawberries, and oranges, as well as other citrus fruits. This is particularly important when you are consuming legumes or other plant-based sources of iron. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ these beverages contain substances that decrease the absorption of iron (and calcium). 

## **Folic Acid:** 

You have probably been taking folic acid supplements before your pregnancy. It is important that you continue taking your folic acid supplements during your pregnancy too. An adequate amount of folic acid is needed in order to decrease the risk of early birth (preterm), or birth defects such as neural tube defects (i.e., improper development of the baby’s brain or spinal cord)[[24]] . 

**You are therefore expected to continue with your folic acid supplementation (400 �����������������������������������������������������������[ [25]]** . In some cases, and depending on your health condition, your doctor may recommend that folic acid supplementation be continued throughout the entire pregnancy[[24]] , or he/she may recommend higher doses. Your doctor will advise you on the right dose for you. 

In addition to folic acid supplementation, it is also important that you consume a diet rich in folate (i.e., folic acid). Table 5 provides tips on what food options are rich sources of folate.

## **Vitamin D:** 

Even though you can meet part of your vitamin D requirement through sunlight exposure, it is also important that you consume foods that are rich in vitamin D. Few foods are naturally rich ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ beef liver also contain vitamin D. However, you are advised to limit the consumption of liver and liver products when you are pregnant, since they contain very high amounts of vitamin A that ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� Below are examples of foods that are considered good sources of vitamin D[[26]] :

- ������������������������������������������� 

In addition to the consumption of foods rich in vitamin D, it is advisable that you get some sun exposure. Some vitamin D researchers in the UK and USA suggest that approximately 5 - 30 minutes of sun exposure between 10 AM and 3 PM at least twice a week to the face, arms, legs, or back without sunscreen is usually enough[ [13, 28]] . Data for estimates are not available in the Middle East, but required exposure time for Qatar is likely less than these estimates[ [13, 28]] . ## **Calcium:** 

The recommendations for calcium intake do not increase during pregnancy. Hence, if you have an adequate dietary intake of calcium, you do not need to take calcium supplements when you are pregnant. Supplementation is recommended only for women who do not consume milk and dairy products, and in certain special cases. That said, it is important that you obtain the recommended 1000 mg/day of calcium from dietary sources. Milk and dairy products are the richest sources of dietary calcium as shown in Table 6. 

Table 6. What is equivalent to the calcium in 1 cup milk (300 mg calcium)? 

- 1 cup yogurt (low fat or skimmed) 

- 50 grams of white low salt cheese

## **Other vitamins and minerals:** 

In addition to iron, folic acid, vitamin D and calcium, your doctor may recommend supplementation with other vitamins and minerals[ [33]] . Although vitamin A is important for the healthy development of your baby, large amounts may cause malformations and birth defects. It is therefore important that you **avoid any supplements containing vitamin A, retinol, as well as supplements ������������������������������������** . Moreover, you are advised **to limit the consumption of liver and liver products due to their very high vitamin A content.** Your doctor should be consulted before considering vitamin A supplementation. 

## **Omega-3 fatty acids:** 

Omega-3 fatty acids are a type of fat that your body cannot make on its own. While these fats are important to be part of everyone’s diet, they are particularly important for you and your baby. Adequate consumption of omega-3 fatty acids provides the building blocks of your baby’s brain and nervous system, and plays a role in preventing maternal depression after childbirth[[34]] . ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� and some varieties of canned tuna (canned, light)[ [13]] . Zobaidy (malabar cavalla) and gubgub (sea ������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������� 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ levels of contaminants such as mercury. For this reason, limit the consumption of king mackerel, ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������ 

�������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� based foods that contain some omega-3 fats. These include walnuts, pumpkin seeds, and other ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ����������������������������������������������������[[13, 15]] . 

In case an adequate dietary intake of omega-3 fatty acids is not achieved, then your doctor may recommend that you take supplements. **Always check with your doctor before taking any supplements.**

- **Vegetarian diet:** this is in general characterized by the exclusion of animal-based products ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� and dairy products, honey, and eggs.

## Box 8. Dietary recommendations for vegetarian and vegan women

- Combine legumes with whole grain cereals in your meals. This will improve the quality of the protein you are consuming. 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� absorption of iron from plant-based foods.

## 3.7. Ramadan fasting during pregnancy 

**Consult your doctor before deciding to fast and follow up closely with a dietitian.** In case you decide to fast during the month of Ramadan, follow the recommendations outlined in Box 9[[35-37]] . 

## Box 9. Recommendations in relation to fasting during the month of Ramadan 

- Do not follow an unhealthy dietary pattern during the month of Ramadan, since this may cause unnecessary weight gain. Excess weight gain during pregnancy could increase your risk of developing gestational diabetes (a form of diabetes that appears during pregnancy). 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� risk of dehydration by avoiding exposure to the sun. 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� soups) during Iftar and Suhoor. 

- Consume a healthy, balanced Iftar, following the recommendation for an adequate and balanced diet as outlined in section 3.1. Below is a simple guide for your meal[[38]] : 

   - Fill ½ of your plate with vegetables. 

   - ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ 

   - Fill the remainder of your plate (¼) with whole grain cereals such as brown rice or brown pasta or whole wheat bread 

   - Add a cup of low-fat, low-salt laban or low-fat yogurt 

   - Add fruit as a snack or you may have 2-3 dates, which is equivalent to one serving of fruits 

- Do not skip Suhoor. 

- Favor whole grain cereals such as whole breads, brown pasta and brown rice and limit your ����������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- Eat slowly and consume small portions to avoid any discomfort and decrease the likelihood of overeating. 

- Limit the use of butter and ghee. 

- Limit high salty and fatty foods. 

- Limit the intake of sweets and replace them with healthier options such as a fruit salad, low-fat and low sugar pudding. 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� as vegetables and fruits (such as tomatoes, avocados, dried fruits, and bananas) during the Suhoor mealtime. 

- Use healthy cooking methods such as baking, steaming, boiling or grilling. 

- Take the supplements recommended by your doctor, with the Iftar and/or Suhoor meals.

## 3.8. Use of herbal supplements/teas during pregnancy 

**==> picture [108 x 82] intentionally omitted <==**

Taking herbal supplements or herbal teas to prevent or treat certain health conditions has long been part of our traditions. However, it is important that you watch out for these supplements or herbal teas during your pregnancy. Even if these products contain natural ingredients, this does not directly mean that they are safe. Some of these herbal supplements or herbal teas may have ingredients that are not listed on the label, and which could pass on to your baby. They may also interfere with other medicines or supplements that you are taking. 

����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� medicinal products. Be cautious when consuming these herbal supplements/teas. As a general rule, it is better to choose herbs that are usually used in cooking and teas made from fruits. Avoid making your own herbal tea from plants you have collected yourself. Large amounts of some herbs may possibly initiate contractions and increase your risk of early labor, or they may ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� to drink. 

Box 10 contains a list of the commonly used herbal teas and their indications /contraindications during pregnancy (Box 10)[[39, 40]] .

## **Use of Medications in Pregnancy** 

Almost every pregnant woman will face a decision about taking medications during her pregnancy. However, it is important to know that not all medications are safe to take during this period. Some medications may cause birth defects, pregnancy loss, premature birth, developmental problems or even infant death[[45]] . 

**==> picture [251 x 271] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Avoiding Harmful Substances** 

During your pregnancy, it is very important to stay away from certain harmful substances that may cause health risks for you or your baby. Among those substances are smoking and energy drinks. 

## 5.1. Smoking 

Smoking decreases the amount of oxygen that reaches your baby and exposes the fetus to chemicals that may cause cancer. It also leads to a greater risk of early birth (preterm birth), miscarriages, having a small baby (low birth weight), or even death. 

Smoking increases your risk of developing diabetes during pregnancy (gestational diabetes). ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� (whether you were the one smoking or you were inhaling the smoke from someone else who is smoking). 

- Cigarette smoking is therefore not safe during pregnancy as it contains nicotine. Nicotine can increase the baby’s heart rate and respiratory infections, delay his/her growth and damage his/her brain and lungs. 

- Shisha is not safe to use during pregnancy since it also contains nicotine. 

- E-cigarettes, vapes and other tobacco products containing nicotine are also not safe to use ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� harmful to the developing baby. 

You are therefore strongly advised to avoid all tobacco-containing products whether through ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� are living with you in the same household, are aware of the risks of smoking. Box 11 presents a few key points with regards to smoking and pregnancy[ [46]] . 

**==> picture [138 x 139] intentionally omitted <==**

## Box 11. Key points with regards to smoking and pregnancy 

- Smoking during pregnancy is harmful to you and your baby. 

- Passive smoking (breathing in other people’s tobacco smoke) can also harm you and your baby. 

- A baby that is born too small due to smoking is not a healthy baby. 

- If you smoke, the best thing you can do is stop. Stopping at any time in pregnancy will ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� down), ideally before getting pregnant. 

- **Shisha smoking** is not safe during pregnancy. 

- E-smoking and any tobacco containing substance are not safe during pregnancy. 

- You and your husband are advised to seek help, advice, and support to stop smoking. 

- Nicotine replacement therapy (NRT) is safe to use in pregnancy. 

## 5.2. Energy Drinks 

��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� dehydration, insomnia, as well as increased blood pressure and heart rate[ [47]] . This may cause health problems for you and your baby[[41-43]] . You should not consume energy drinks during your pregnancy.

## **Pregnancy Related Concerns: Nausea, Vomiting, Constipation and Heartburn** 

It is not uncommon that you experience gastrointestinal (GI) issues during your pregnancy. As the baby grows, less space is available in the abdomen for your intestines, stomach, and ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� are resolved after delivery. The most common pregnancy-related health concerns are nausea, vomiting, constipation, and heartburn. 

## 6.1. Nausea and vomiting 

During your early pregnancy, you may be experiencing episodes of nausea and vomiting, often known as morning sickness. The common perception is that morning sickness happens only in the morning; however, it can happen at any time of the day or night or could last for the whole day. �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� and severity usually decline by weeks 16 to 20 of your pregnancy. The recommendations described in Box 12 can help you manage nausea and vomiting[[48-50]] . 

## Box 12. Tips to help manage nausea and vomiting during pregnancy 

- Have small, frequent meals every 1–2 hours. 

- Limit drinking during your meals. 

- Drink small sips of water to stay hydrated and minimize nausea. 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� not contain hydrogenated oils, etc.), high protein foods (boiled egg, turkey slices) or plain yogurt. 

- Restrict the consumption of foods that have strong odors. 

- Limit the consumption fatty and spicy foods. 

- ����������������������������������������������������������� 

- Ask your doctor if you can take vitamin B6 supplements or other antiemetic medications (drugs that treat nausea and vomiting). 

- **If symptoms persist, discuss your symptoms with a doctor.** 

**==> picture [73 x 45] intentionally omitted <==**

## 6.2. Constipation 

During your pregnancy, you may experience more frequent constipation episodes. Constipation means having fewer than 3 bowel motions per week and having stools that are hard to pass. However, constipation will often resolve itself as pregnancy progresses and after delivery. Your �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� and is not passed on to the baby. However, constipation may reduce your quality of life and perception of your health as well as increase the risk of haemorrhoids[[51]] . Box 13 lists a few tips for you to prevent constipation and reduce its symptoms[ [48, 52-54]] . 

## Box 13. Tips to help manage constipation during pregnancy 

- �������������������������������������� 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� protein. 

- Do some light physical activity to help enhance the bowel movement. 

- **If symptoms persist, discuss your symptoms with a healthcare provider.** 

## 6.3. Heartburn 

Heartburn is very common during pregnancy[[55]] . It rarely leads to serious complications, and it usually resolves soon after delivery. Your doctor may recommend that you take certain medications that decrease the acidity in the stomach (antacids). In addition, the following recommendations may help you reduce the discomfort and symptoms of heartburn (Box 14)[[48, ] 49, 52]. 

## Box 14. Tips to help decrease heartburn during pregnancy 

- Have small, frequent meals. 

- ��������������������������������������������� 

- Eat and chew slowly. 

- Limit the consumption of very spicy foods. 

- �������������������������������������������������� 

- Limit fried and greasy foods. 

- Limit citrus foods, tomatoes and mint. 

**==> picture [121 x 122] intentionally omitted <==**

- Do not lay down immediately after eating. 

- Use more pillows to raise your head and shoulders when lying down. 

- **If symptoms persist, discuss your symptoms with a healthcare provider.**

**Physical Activity Recommendations During Pregnancy** 

## 7.1. Pregnancy and Physical Activity – Is it safe? 

Once you announce your pregnancy and your intention to be physically active, you might face ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� the most important” or “exercise will not leave enough nutrients for the baby.” 

The above fears are passed on from generation to generation and are based on outdated guidelines from the 1950s and earlier[[56]] . Ever since the 1980s, science has debunked the myths with facts. 

Modern science is taking your side. “Physical activity and exercise in pregnancy are associated ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� to exercise routines may be necessary because of normal anatomic and physiologic changes and fetal requirements.”[ [57]]

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
It is safe to be physically<br>Remember active throughout a healthy<br>pregnancy, however, any intense<br>exercise regime should be<br>discussed with your family doctor.<br>For more information refer to<br>section 7.3.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## ������������� 

Despite misconceptions, it is important to know that physical activity during pregnancy not ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� exercise habits and intensity are necessary because of the many changes that are taking place in your body during pregnancy. 

��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [58]] : 

- Minimizing morning sickness 

- Back pain and swelling of the legs and feet 

- Maintaining a healthy body weight 

- �������������������������������������������� 

- ���������������������� 

- Improving your ability to do everyday activities 

- Improving your heart health 

- Controlling blood sugar levels, blood pressure and improving blood lipids (increasing levels of good cholesterol (HDL) and decreasing triglycerides levels) 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ and some types of cancer 

- Enhancing the function of your digestive system 

- Improving your overall well-being and quality of life 

- Lowering stress levels 

- Reducing episodes of depression 

- Improving breathing 

- Improving immunity 

- Enhancing sleep quality 

- Facilitating postpartum weight loss and recovery 

- Reducing the risk of infant obesity, while improving the cardiovascular system, nervous system development and brain development 

## 7.3. Recommendations and contraindications to exercise during pregnancy 

The general recommendation is that you perform a cumulative of 40-60 minutes of low to moderate-intensity physical activity for at least 5 days/week. Vigorous-intensity activities are not encouraged during pregnancy[ [58]] .

## **If you regularly engaged in vigorous physical activity, or were physically active prior** 

**to your pregnancy** , you can continue being active at this intensity level throughout your pregnancy. Still, you should coordinate your exercise regime with your healthcare specialist and seek clearance. Be responsible and do not aim for new records and exhausting exercise sessions. ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� So, the best advice will be to always listen to your body and avoid some sorts of exercises altogether (see Box 15 for detailed tips on how to be careful while exercising). 

## Box 15. Be careful while exercising 

- **Don’t bump your belly!** You want to avoid contact sports and risky physical activities such as martial arts (sparring), football, or horseback riding to reduce the risk of your baby belly getting hit. 

- **Avoid the extreme!** For the upcoming 9 months skip your skiing vacation (above 2500 m altitude) and delay your scuba diving experience to another time. The change in air pressure might be harmful for your baby. 

- **Control your movements!** The production of the hormone relaxin increases in preparation for giving birth[[59]] ����������������������������������������������������������� ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� changes. Engage in an extended warmup and cool down routine. This will decrease your ��������������� 

- **Drink a lot of water!** Always carry a water bottle with you and drink, before, during �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� The exercise itself does not lead to dangerous levels of heat, but you should avoid the hot summer outdoors. 

- **Posture Control!** Over time, but usually around 16 weeks, you will notice a change in body posture, leading to an arching in your back. This might result in lower back pain. Staying physically active and strengthening your core can help. Be careful when strengthening your core at this time and avoid lying on your back. About 10% of expecting women experience low blood pressure while lying on their backs. 

**In case you had a sedentary lifestyle before pregnancy,** you may wish to start by doing ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� cycling, water aerobics (or aqua gym), swimming and Pilates. 

Below are a few recommendations you may wish to consider regarding your physical activity during pregnancy: 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� gradually increase the exercise duration. You have plenty of time to work on your speed and distance once you established a routine. Start by walking 15 minutes every other day then increase the time by 5 minutes every week until you reach the recommended 40 minutes. Try to exercise on most of the days before you gradually increase the intensity. 

- To bring the activity to a suitable intensity level, try the “talk test” where you should still be able to talk while doing the activity. In case you are not able to maintain a conversation then you should reduce the pace at which you are exercising (for more details on the talk test, refer to Box 16 below).

## **Oral Health** 

food particles and acids that forms on the teeth and can lead to dental decay and gum disease). Gum disease in pregnant women may lead to premature birth (early birth) and low birth weight (very small baby). Thus you are highly encouraged to practice good oral hygiene habits[ [63, 64]] : 

- 

- Floss your teeth once daily. 

- Limit foods containing sweets as they may stick to your teeth and cause dental caries. 

- Drink water or low-fat milk, while limiting sugar-sweetened beverages. 

- Eat fruits rather than drinking fruit juices. 

- Receive the necessary oral treatment before delivery if possible. 

- The period between the 14th and the 20th week of pregnancy (2nd trimester) is the best time to receive any treatment (including dental X-rays). However, necessary treatments can still be provided throughout pregnancy, including treatments for urgent conditions requiring immediate care during the 1st trimester. 

- Visit the dentist twice a year, or more if needed. 

If you are experiencing morning sickness, including vomiting, some of the stomach acid will be left on your teeth. This acid could be harmful as it increases your risk of tooth erosion and dental decay. In this case, you are encouraged to follow the below recommendations[ [63, 64]] : 

- Eat small portions of nutritious meals/snacks throughout the day. 

- Chew sugar free or Xylitol-containing gum after meals. 

- Thoroughly brush your teeth and rinse with a mouthwash that you can buy at the pharmacy (you can also prepare a homemade mouthwash using a teaspoon of baking soda (sodium bicarbonate) in a cup of water can help). 

- Refrain from brushing the teeth until 30 minutes after vomiting to prevent damage of tooth structure.

## **Emotional Health and Wellness** 

��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� your physical health. If you are mentally healthy, you will be in the best position to manage the challenges of pregnancy and life with a new baby. 

��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� proportion of pregnant women during pregnancy and after delivery. These mental health issues may lead to poor health for the mother, father, and infant. While some women overcome their mental health problems, many develop chronic conditions. It is always advisable to get in contact �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� episodes, worry, fear, being overwhelmed, anger, moodiness, , and trouble sleeping. 

Box 18 below lists some strategies that can help you care for your emotional wellbeing. 

Box 18. Tips to help pregnant women care for their emotional wellbeing 

- Connect with family and friends. 

- Exercise regularly, when applicable (Refer to section 7). 

- ��������������������������

## 9.1. Sleep during pregnancy 

As you progress through your pregnancy, you could be experiencing a few symptoms that may ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ pain, fetal movement, leg cramps, and heartburn. In addition, if you had a sleep disorder before your pregnancy (such as sleep-disordered breathing), this disorder may worsen when you get pregnant[ [65]] . 

Box 19 includes some tips to manage sleep disturbances and improve your quality of sleep[[66]] . It is advisable to discuss with your doctor if insomnia, sleep apnea or any other condition is interfering with your sleep. 

## Box 19. Tips to manage sleep disturbances and improve your  quality of sleep 

- Favor your side: Try to avoid sleeping on your back, which can put the weight of your uterus on your back. 

- Use pillows: Placing a pillow between your bent knees or under your belly may help you get comfortable when laying down. 

- Follow sleep hygiene recommendations, as per the below: 

   - Keep a cool, dark, quiet bedroom. 

   - Adhere to a consistent bedtime. In case you wanted to nap, try to do so earlier in the day so it won’t interfere with nighttime sleep. 

   - Indulge in calming activities (reading a book, taking a warm bath) in preparation for bedtime. 

   - Use a dim nightlight to make it easier to get back to sleep after going to the bathroom. 

   - ����������������������������������������������������������������� 

   - Avoid exposure to blue light (screens of TV, tablets, or smart phones) at least an hour before bed. 

   - Get regular exercise earlier in the day. 

   - Reduce liquid intake before bed to reduce nighttime bathroom breaks, but drink plenty of water throughout the day. 

   - If you cannot sleep, get out of bed and do something else until you feel sleepy. 

**==> picture [132 x 132] intentionally omitted <==**

## 9.2. Eating disorders during pregnancy 

��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� (abnormal fear of food with an abnormally low weight), bulimia nervosa (eating large amounts of food followed by self-induced vomiting) and binge eating (consuming large amounts of food in a small amount of time). Because the age range for these eating disorders overlaps with the age range of becoming pregnant, it is not unusual for a pregnant woman to be experiencing an eating disorder. 

Eating disorders can occur as a consequence of pregnancy (because of the change in body shape) or it can develop before pregnancy, with the pregnancy further complicating the symptoms of eating disorders. 

While many women are not aware whether or not they have an eating disorder, it is important to discuss with your doctor if you experience any of the following: 

- Spending a lot of time worrying about your weight and body shape 

- Avoiding socializing when food is involved 

- Not eating enough 

- Exercising too much (excessively) 

- Having very strict habits or routines around food 

Bear in mind that eating disorders may lead to serious health consequences during pregnancy such as maternal depression and anxiety, abnormal development of the baby, pregnancy and delivery complications, premature birth (early birth), low birth weight (very small baby), risk of miscarriage and low breastmilk supply (after childbirth). Hence it is a priority to seek medical care if you suspect having any eating disorders.

**==> picture [35 x 53] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Food Safety Considerations During Pregnancy** 

## 10.1. Safe food preparation, handling, and storage 

During pregnancy, your body naturally undergoes hormonal changes, some of which change the immune system itself and therefore increases your risk of foodborne illness (i.e., illnesses caused by consuming contaminated food or beverage). For detailed information on food safety considerations, including food purchase and handling, please refer to Appendix 2. 

It is important that you do not consume undercooked foods during your pregnancy. Table 11 ��������������������������������������������������������������[[67]] . 

|Food<br>Safe Minimum Temperature<br>�����������������������������������������������������|Food<br>Safe Minimum Temperature<br>�����������������������������������������������������|
|---|---|
|52<br>Beef, veal, lamb<br>Steaks, roasts, chops<br>Chicken and turkey, whole<br>Poultry breasts, roasts<br>Poultry thighs, legs, wings<br>Shrimp, lobster and crabs<br>Eggs<br>Egg dishes<br>Clams, oysters and mussels<br>����������������������������<br>Scallops<br>71°C<br>63°C<br>74°C<br>������������������������������<br>���������������������������<br>71°C<br>Cook until shells open during cooking<br>���������������������������<br>and separates easily with a fork<br>���������������������������������������||



## ����������������������������� 

During your pregnancy, your immune system may be a little weaker as compared to before pregnancy, hence placing you and your baby at a higher risk of foodborne illnesses. These illnesses can lead to miscarriage or premature delivery (early delivery). 

Some foodborne illnesses, such as listeriosis (infection with Listeria) and toxoplasmosis (infection with Toxoplasma gondii), can infect your baby even if you do not feel sick. Below are further details about these two harmful organisms: 

- **Listeria:** Harmful germs found in many foods, including ready-to-eat refrigerated foods like deli meats, unpasteurized (raw) milk, soft cheeses made with unpasteurized milk. Listeriosis may cause miscarriage, premature delivery (early delivery), stillbirth and serious sickness. 

- **Toxoplasma gondii:** A parasite found in many food sources such as raw and undercooked meats, unwashed vegetables and contaminated water. Toxoplasma gondii can cause hearing loss, blindness and brain damage in babies. 

Table 12 provides you with a list of high risk foods (that you need to limit) and lower risk foods (that you need to favor)[ [67]] . Lower risk food options should be chosen. 

|Table 12. Higher risk and lower risk food options for pregnant women|Table 12. Higher risk and lower risk food options for pregnant women|
|---|---|
|Higher risk foods<br>Lower risk foods||
|Soft cheeses made from unpasteurized (raw) milk|Hard cheeses. Soft cheeses only if they are made<br>from pasteurized milk|
|������������������������������������������<br>unpasteurized apple cider|����������������������|
|Refrigerated smoked seafood and raw or<br>undercooked seafood|�����������������������|
|����������������������������������<br>non-vegetarian sushi<br>��������������������������������|������������������������������|
|Undercooked meat, poultry|Fully cooked lean meats and poultry|
|Sandwiches with cold deli or luncheon meat|Grilled sandwiches in which the meat or poultry is<br>heated until steaming|
|Soft-boiled or “over-easy” eggs, as the yolks are not<br>fully cooked|�����������������������������������|
|Salads, wraps or sandwiches containing raw<br>(uncooked) or lightly cooked sprouts|Salads, wraps or sandwiches containing cooked<br>sprouts|

## **Importance of Having a Strong Family Support System** 

Ensuring the best for the baby’s health is not only your responsibility, but also that of the father too. Family and social support including the husband’s support and involvement play an important ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [68]] . 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ pregnancy. 

## ������������������������������������������������������������������ 

- Go together to the doctor’s visits. 

- Discuss together decisions about prenatal tests, such as those for birth defects. 

- Get his support in making lifestyle changes. He may decide to give up smoking for example. This can be a good time for both of you to make some lifestyle changes that you have been thinking about. 

- Encourage him to eat healthy foods; this can support you in making better and healthier choices as well. 

- Talk to your husband about your need to take breaks and naps. Hormones during pregnancy can change a woman’s energy level and need for sleep. 

- Take walks together. It gives you exercise and time to talk. 

In addition to your husband’s support, that of family and friends also play an important role in helping you adhere to a healthy lifestyle throughout your pregnancy.

**Gestational Diabetes Mellitus (GDM) During Pregnancy** ��������������������������������������� 

Gestational Diabetes Mellitus (GDM) is a health condition that occurs during pregnancy when ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� and reach the baby. GDM might complicate the pregnancy and put both the mother and baby, at possible health risks, especially if blood sugar levels are not well controlled[ [69]] . 

## 12.1. Factors that increase the risk of GDM 

Certain factors may increase your risk of GDM (Box 21). If you have any of those factors, it is recommended that you adhere to the recommendations outlined in section 12.4 in this chapter. 

## Box 21. Factors that increase your risk of GDM during pregnancy 

- Being overweight or obese before pregnancy 

- Being 35 years old or more 

- Having GDM in previous pregnancies 

- Having one of the family members with type II diabetes (mother, father, sibling, etc.) 

- If any of your pre-pregnancy blood results were abnormal for glucose 

- History of unexplained fetal or neonatal death, or birth of baby with malformations 

- �������������������������������������������������������������� 

- Having a health condition that may increase the risk of diabetes such as polycystic ovarian syndrome (PCOS), hypertension, cardiovascular diseases, or the use of glucocorticoid hormones (such as cortisone). 

**==> picture [123 x 136] intentionally omitted <==**

## 12.2. Health risks associated with GDM 

While GDM is concerning, it is important for you to know that this condition is controllable. You can in fact control and maintain your blood sugar within normal range by eating healthy foods, exercising and if necessary, taking  prescribed medication (see section 12.5). If properly ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� GDM may result in many negative health consequences as outlined in Box 22, below. 

## Box 22. Risk of uncontrolled GDM on the mother and baby 

- High blood pressure, water retention and loss of protein in urine • Increased possibility of early birth, i.e., before 37 weeks 

- Risks on • Increased possibility of caesarian section 

- mother • Higher chances of experiencing a miscarriage • Elevated risk of developing type II diabetes in the future 

- Increased possibility of being larger in size than what is recommended 

- Risks on • Increased risk of birth defects and stillbirth 

- baby • Elevated risk of developing obesity and type II diabetes later in life 

## 12.3. When and how to test for GDM 

If you do not have a history of diabetes, you will be asked to test for GDM at 24–28 weeks of pregnancy. The test for GDM is called Oral Glucose Tolerance Test (OGTT). This test will ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� You need to do this test following an overnight fast of at least 8 hours. If diagnosed with GDM, then you will need to visit your doctor every 1-3 weeks for check-ups. 

It is important to know that, if you have developed GDM during your pregnancy, your blood sugar will generally return to normal levels soon after delivery. However, you should keep checking your blood sugar regularly, at least every 3 years, to screen for prediabetes or diabetes. 

## 12.4. Prevention of GDM 

The prevention of GDM relies on 3 main rules, as follows: 

**==> picture [242 x 58] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
1 2<br>3<br>Maintain a healthy  Choose an<br>Maintain an active<br>body weight gain  adequate<br>lifestyle<br>throughout the  and balanced diet<br>pregnancy<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## **1- Maintain a healthy body weight before and during pregnancy** 

By controlling your weight gain during pregnancy, you minimize your risk of developing GDM. Refer to section 2 in this chapter for more information on weight gain recommendations during pregnancy. 

## **2- Choose a healthy adequate and balanced diet** 

A balanced and adequate diet should be an important part of your healthy lifestyle as it helps prevent many diseases, including GDM. Refer to section 3 in this chapter for detailed description of the healthy diet to be followed during your pregnancy. 

## **3- Maintain an active lifestyle** 

�������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� have a physically active lifestyle to help you reduce the risk of GDM. Engaging in physical activity can also help you decrease common discomforts of pregnancy (such as back pain), without having a negative impact on you or your baby. Refer to section 7.2 of this chapter for physical activity recommendations and practical tips 

While aiming for an active lifestyle, it is important for you to stay hydrated by drinking water before, during and after exercising. Also, it is important for you to avoid exercising in a hot and humid environment. 

## 12.5. Management of GDM 

If diagnosed with GDM, you will be receiving all needed guidance and assistance from your doctor to better understand the results of your blood tests and to develop skills to self-manage your condition. It is strongly recommended that you discuss your concerns and emotions with ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ recommended range and that you are adhering to an adequate and balanced diet. These are explained in the sections below: 

## **12.5.1 Weight gain within recommended range** 

While achieving and maintaining proper weight gain during pregnancy are important recommendations for all pregnant women, they are critical for you, in case you were diagnosed with GDM. Pregnant women with GDM are strongly encouraged to adhere to the following acceptable weight gain recommendations to minimize the risk of complications (Table 13). 

|Table 13. Acceptable weight gain for pregnant women with GDM|Table 13. Acceptable weight gain for pregnant women with GDM|Table 13. Acceptable weight gain for pregnant women with GDM|
|---|---|---|
|BMI category<br>��������<br>< 20 weeks<br>Acceptable weight gain by gestation period|||

|Normal<br>(18.5-24.9  kg/m2)|4.0 - 5.5 kg|7.5 - 10.5 kg|
|Overweight<br>(25-29.9  kg/m2)|2.0 - 3.0 kg|5.0 - 8.0 kg|
|Obese<br>��������2)|0 kg|5.0 - 9.0 kg for Class I obese<br>(BMI between 30 and 34.9 kg/m2)|

Adapted from the Institute of Medicine, Food and Nutrition Board, Committee on Nutritional Status During Pregnancy. 

## **12.5.2 Balanced dietary intake** 

Eating a balanced diet is a critical part of your treatment plan for GDM. A balanced diet includes a variety of foods from all the six food groups, providing you and your baby with all the essential nutrients, vitamins, and minerals that you need. Eating a balanced diet will also help you keep your blood sugar levels in the healthy target range. It is essential that you follow-up with a ����������������������������������������������������������� 

Following your diagnosis, you may be particularly concerned about your carbohydrate intake, ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ are an essential component of a healthy diet, even for women with GDM. Not getting enough carbohydrates can cause serious problems for you and your baby. You should therefore follow the carbohydrate intake recommendations and meal plan provided by a dietitian. Box 23 presents some essential information that you need to know about carbohydrates. 

Box 23. Essential information that you need to know about carbohydrates 

- Carbohydrates are nutrients that come from starchy foods, like bread, pasta, and rice. They are also found in milk and yogurt, starchy vegetables (such as potatoes, corn, butternut squash, turnips, and beets) and fruits. 

- When eaten, carbohydrates are broken down in your body into simple sugars, which your body uses as a source of energy. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� a small amount of carbohydrate at a meal, your blood sugar level increases by a small amount. If you eat a large amount of carbohydrate at a meal, your blood sugar level increases by a large amount. 

- It is important to include a carbohydrate-rich food in each meal and snack while paying attention to your portion size. 

- Choose whole grain cereals (such as whole breads, brown pasta and brown rice, ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ 

- • Certain carbohydrates raise blood glucose more than others, even when both are consumed in the same amounts. These carbohydrates are known to have a higher ‘glycemic index’. 

   - Examples of high glycemic index carbohydrates are added sugars, sweetened foods and beverages, white bread, breakfast cereals, fatayer, potatoes 

   - On the other hand, foods with ‘low glycemic index’ do not increase blood glucose as much, such as legumes. 

   - In addition to the carbohydrate counting strategy (explained below), you can also �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� blood sugar). This can be decided with a dietitian. For a listing of high, intermediate and low glycemic index foods, please refer to Table 15 below[[70, 71]] . 

**==> picture [146 x 137] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [148 x 153] intentionally omitted <==**

There are a few recommendations that will guide you on how to plan your diet for a better control of GDM. These recommendations are discussed below: 

## **1. Start counting carbohydrates.** 

Counting your carbohydrates can be a very useful tool in helping you understand and achieve the right amount of carbohydrates intake. It will also help you distribute the amount of carbohydrates that you need to consume over your daily meals. 

The exact amount of carbohydrates in grams that you need to include in your diet will depend on your energy needs, activity level, and blood glucose control.  It will be determined by a dietitian. Overall, your carbohydrates requirements will likely be around 40-45 grams for each meal (3 meals) and 15-30 grams per snack (a dietitian will determine the number of snacks you need to eat during the day) 

To be able to count the number of grams of carbohydrate at each meal and snack you will need to: 

- Learn from with a dietitian about the various carbohydrate food sources and the ������������������������������������������������������ 

- Read the nutrition labels or learn to estimate the number of grams of carbohydrate in the foods you eat (Table 14). A dietitian will help you in building these skills.

## **2. Eat smaller amounts of carbohydrates at each meal.** 

Distribute your carbohydrates over your meals throughout the day, instead of eating �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� snacks throughout the day will help to keep your blood sugar under control. 

## **3. Include protein in your meals and snacks.** 

You need more proteins in your diet when you are pregnant, especially during the third trimester. Research shows that protein when consumed with carbohydrates can help regulate your blood glucose. Protein may also help you feel fuller throughout the day. 

## **4. Limit sugar and concentrated sweets.** 

It is recommended that you limit desserts and sugar-sweetened beverages as they tend to ��������������������������������������������������� 

����������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- b. Limit desserts such as ice cream, pies, cakes, and cookies. 

- c. Read nutrition labels carefully and check them for total carbohydrates per serving.

In addition to these recommendations, there are a few nutritional recommendations for you to consider when planning your diet. Box 24 below provides nutritional recommendations and guidelines for pregnant women with GDM. 

## Box 24. Nutritional recommendations for pregnant women with GDM 

- Maintaining an appropriate energy intake, adequate amounts, and types of carbohydrates ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� GDM. 

- Relying mainly on **��������** carbohydrates in the diet (whole grain bread, brown rice, quinoa, barley, oats, legumes, vegetables, and whole fruits). 

- Taking a multivitamin or mineral supplement may be required if certain minerals or vitamins are ����������������������������������������������������������� 

- Depending on your current eating habits, gestational weight gain and blood glucose levels, ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� potassium (Ace-K), sucralose, neotame, aspartame and steviol glycosides) are usually poor in �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

   - ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� sweeteners from time to time 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� side since saccharin can cross the placenta and reach the baby) 

- It is also better to limit foods and beverages that were sweetened with aspartame if you have a family history of phenylketonuria (an inherited metabolic disorder). 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� new on the market. 

Please note that, together with a dietitian and doctor, you will have an individualized meal plan. This plan will take into consideration your energy and nutrients requirement and the type of medication you are currently taking (if any). 

## **12.5.3 Blood glucose monitoring** 

��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� of GDM. This is strongly recommended since high blood glucose levels (at fasting or after a ��������������������������������������������������������������������[[72]] . 

You will be taught by your doctor how to monitor your blood glucose levels on your own. For this, you will need to have a reliable and calibrated glucometer at home (i.e., a small device that �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� you will be instructed to test 4 times per day (during the fasting state and 1-2 hours after each meal)[[73]] . If you were taking insulin, however, you will be recommended to test 6-7 times per day (during the fasting state, pre-meals, 1-2 hours after each meal, and before bedtime). 

Your goals for blood glucose levels should be individualized and will be set following discussion with your doctor. In general, the glucose targets are as follows[ [73-75]] : 

- Fasting blood glucose: < 95 mg/dL (5.3 mmol/L) 

- After a meal: 

   - ����������������������������������������������������������� 

## OR 

- Blood glucose 2-hours after a meal: < 120 mg/dL (6.7 mmol/L) 

## **12.5.4 Treatment with insulin or medications for GDM** 

�������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ��������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [72, 73]] . Your doctor will provide you with details about your insulin therapy. Box 25 below provides you with some tips if you were on insulin therapy[[72]] . 

**==> picture [115 x 111] intentionally omitted <==**

Box 25. Tips for pregnant women on insulin therapy 

- Maintain carbohydrate consistency at meals and snacks in order to facilitate insulin ������������ 

- Learn about the signs and symptoms of hypoglycemia (low blood glucose) and ways to ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- Make sure to use medications as prescribed. 

## **12.5.5 Additional recommendations for women with GDM** 

In addition to consuming a healthy and balanced diet, it is also important for you to take care of your mental health and wellbeing during pregnancy. For this consult section 9 in this chapter. ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� Refer to section 5 within this chapter for more information. Similarly, you need to watch out for the safety of the food you consume to prevent the development of food poisoning or other illnesses (consult section 10). 

In addition, recommendations regarding supplementation and oral health are given in sections 3.5 and 8 above, while section 6 provides you with recommendations on how to deal with the most common pregnancy-related health concerns which are nausea, vomiting, constipation, and heartburn. Finally, make sure to consult your doctor regarding fasting in Ramadan if you have GDM. 

## **APPENDIX 1:** 

BODY WEIGHT CLASSIFICATION ACCORDING TO BMI (BEFORE PREGNANCY) 

Body Mass Index (BMI) is a measure of weight relative to height. There are many online calculators that can help determine your BMI. Alternatively, you can book an appointment with a dietitian at your primary healthcare center or at a private clinic to learn more about your BMI. ������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [76]] . ## **APPENDIX 2:** 

FOOD SAFETY CONSIDERATIONS, INCLUDING FOOD PURCHASE AND HANDLING (DURING PREGNANCY) 

Box 1 outlines a few tips to assist you in shopping for safe food. 

Box 1. Tips for safe food purchase 

- Purchase food from reliable sources 

- Read the “Product Label” for food safety information on all foods and beverages. 

- Put raw seafood, poultry, or meat in separate plastic bags. 

- Pick up perishable foods last, and plan to go directly home from the grocery store. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ have been treated to control harmful bacteria. 

- Always purchase refrigerated shell eggs. 

- Do not buy food displayed in unsafe or unclean conditions. 

- Always check the expiry date of the food to be purchased: 

   - A “Sell-By” or “expiry date - EXP” date tells the store how long to display the product for sale. You should buy the product before the date expires. 

   - ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� purchase or safety date. 

   - A “Use-By” date is the last date recommended for the use of the product while at peak quality. The date has been determined by the manufacturer of the product. 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� handling and consumption. These practices fall under the following four categories: Clean, Separate, Cook and Chill. More details about these practices are outlined in Box 2[[77]] . 

**==> picture [139 x 139] intentionally omitted <==**

|Box 2. Tips|for proper food handling|
|---|---|
|**Clean:**|• Wash your hands, before, during and after food preparation and consumption.|
||• Wash your hands for at least 60 seconds.|
||• Practice good personal hygiene during food handling and preparation activities.|
||• ������������������������������������������������������������������|
||tabletops, cooking surfaces and the sink with hot, soapy water before you cook|
||�������������������������������������������������������������������|
||• ������������������������������������������������������������������|
||Vinegar may also be used to disinfect vegetables and fruits.|
||• Limit washing eggs, raw meat and poultry since washing causes bacteria to spread|
||faster. Instead, pat the eggs with a clean, damp towel, and the raw meat and|
||poultry with clean utensils or a damp towel as well.|
||• Wipe food packaging with soap and water before opening, especially lids of cans|
||��������|
|**Separate:**|• Keep cooked and ready-to-eat foods away from raw seafood, poultry, meat, and|
||eggs in the refrigerator and while cooking. (Juices from raw seafood, poultry,|
||meats and cracked eggs can contaminate ready-to-eat foods, so it is important to|
||separate them.)|
||• Ensure that cooked and ready-to-eat foods are placed on top shelves, while raw|
||foods are placed on lower shelves in the refrigerator, in order to prevent the|
||transfer of bacteria from the raw foods to the cooked foods.|
||• If possible, use separate sets of knives, cutting boards, and utensils for seafood,|
||poultry, meat, and eggs. Ensure to wash them in hot, soapy water or in the|
||dishwasher between uses.|
||• Plates that touch raw foods are not safe to reuse for cooked foods until they have|
||been washed. Use clean plates to hold cooked foods, and wash plates thoroughly|
||in hot, soapy water after they touch raw foods.|



**==> picture [153 x 163] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
70<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


**==> picture [80 x 80] intentionally omitted <==**

- **Cook:** • Use clean water. • Cook all food thoroughly: • Food thermometer must be used to measure the internal temperature of cooked foods. Check the internal temperature in several places to make sure that the seafood, poultry, meat or egg product is cooked to safe minimum internal temperatures. 

- • For microwave or oven cooking: always cover food, stir, and rotate for even cooking. 

- • Consume leftovers within 3-4 days. • Reheat leftovers only once. If leftovers are not consumed after being reheated, throw them out. 

- **Chill:** • ������������������������������������������������������������������������������ ��������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- • Limit keeping food at room temperature for more than 2 hours. 

In addition to the above recommendations for food purchase and handling, there are a few general guidelines that will help reduce the risk of foodborne illnesses, as follows: 

- Protect food from insects, rodents, and other animals. 

- Store non-perishable food products in a safe place. 

- Do not eat or drink foods containing raw eggs, or raw unpasteurized milk and unpasteurized ������������ 

- You cannot tell by looking, smelling, or even tasting a food whether it contains pathogens. Yet these pathogens-like disease-causing bacteria, viruses or parasites can make you sick. 

- You should never taste a food to determine if it is safe to eat.
