17<br>Food Allergies<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


What is a food allergy? 

It is an abnormal body response to a certain food or beverage[[38]] . 

How can I reduce the risk of my child having a food allergy? 

You cannot prevent your child from developing a certain food allergy, but studies have shown that following the below recommendations can prevent or delay food allergies in infants: 

- �������������������������������������������������������� 

- Do not begin complementary feeding before six months of age[[38]] (unless medically prescribed by your healthcare provider). 

Allergies to infant formula: 

Breastmilk is the best milk for your baby. If for any reason the baby is switched to cow’s milkbased infant formula, and you found out that the baby is allergic to it then consult the doctor or dietitian for advice on other options such as soy milk. If the infant was also found to be allergic to soy milk, then a special hypoallergenic formula is usually recommended. 

There is no evidence that soy or goat-based formula will reduce the risk of developing allergic diseases in healthy infants. 

What are the most common allergens in the diet? 

When infants are introduced to complementary feeding, some may develop allergies to certain foods. Around 90% of all food allergies are caused by the following types of foods[ [38, 39]] : 

- Animal-based milk such as cow’s milk 

- Eggs 

- Peanuts 

- Soy 

- Tree nuts 

- Fish 

- ����������������������������������� 

- Wheat 

**==> picture [172 x 86] intentionally omitted <==**

- Seeds 

When introducing foods to the baby, especially those foods that are known to cause allergic reactions (as listed above), make sure to introduce each type of food, one at a time, and in small amounts, so you will be able to notice any reactions or symptoms in your baby[[39]] . Do not be scared to introduce these types of foods to your child. In fact, there is no need to limit any of ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� diet[[39]] . 

Some individuals can have allergies for food additives including colors and preservatives, but allergic reactions from ordinary food items are usually more common[ [39]] . 

What are the symptoms of food allergies? 

An allergic reaction can begin within minutes to an hour after ingesting the food or beverage that �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� more symptoms. The most common symptoms of food allergy are[ [38]] : 

- Diarrhea 

- Vomiting 

- Cough 

- Swelling 

- Dry and itchy skin (Eczema) 

- Itching or swelling of the lips, tongue, or mouth 

- Itching or tightness in the throat 

- Skin rashes 

- Sore, red and/or itchy eyes 

- Runny or blocked nose 

- Lowered blood pressure 

- Stomach cramps and pain 

- Red itchy bumps on the skin (Hives) 

- Trouble breathing or shortness of breath 

- Wheezing (coarse sound when breathing) 

**==> picture [165 x 165] intentionally omitted <==**

In some cases, severe allergic reaction may occur, known as “anaphylaxis”; this can be lifethreating[[39, 40]] ������������������������������������������������������������������������������� �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [38]] . Take care when introducing new foods and closely observe whether your child develops any allergic reaction to a newly introduced food. 

How do we diagnose a food allergy? 

A diagnosis should be done by a doctor. You should not make the diagnosis yourself to limit any unnecessary dietary restrictions. In case a food allergy is diagnosed, you must have a dietary plan to replace the eliminated food items, and you also need to have a plan in case of emergency [41]. If your infant/child develops any of the typical allergy-related symptoms after eating any type of food or beverage, you should immediately contact the doctor. 

**==> picture [145 x 145] intentionally omitted <==**

Nutritional concerns in infants and children with food allergies 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ Therefore, it is important to keep in mind that eliminating a certain food group (because of �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� growth problems in your child[ [42]] . 

For example, milk, eggs and soy are good sources of fat and protein. Eliminating these food items �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� are not replaced by other good sources[ [42]] . 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� certain vitamins, which can lead to poor growth. 

- Diets that are low in protein may also lead to protein malnutrition and hence poor growth[[42]] . 

Another example is wheat. This cereal provides the body with carbohydrates, which are known to be an important source of energy for your child’s body, and particularly the brain. Wheat also contains important vitamins and minerals. So if the child is allergic to wheat, other alternative �����������������������������������������������������������������������������[[42]] . 

Another potential challenge is that children that have one or more food allergies might experience some dietary behavior problems more than other children. For example, they may develop “food aversion” (i.e., refusing certain types of food) or a state of anxiety about food, which again can lead to inadequate food intake[ [42]] . 

This is why it is very important that the doctor monitors the growth of infants and children with food allergies[[42]] . It is also important that the doctor or dietitian provide the right alternatives to �����������������������������������������������������������������[[42]] .  The doctor may sometimes prescribe supplements when needed[[42]] . 

What should I do if my child was diagnosed with a food allergy? 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ food or beverage that causes the allergic reaction[ [38, 40, 41, 43]] . It is therefore important to get the help of a dietitian to plan an adequate, healthy and balanced diet for your child, to avoid any �������������������������������������������������������������������������������[[43]] . Below are some practical tips that can help you in managing your child’s food allergy: 

- Check with your dietitian and doctor to  identify food alternatives or nutritional supplements ���������������������[[38]] . 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� item[[41]] . 

- Educate your family (at home) and teachers (in the nursery) about your child’s allergies and what to do in case of an emergency[ [41]] . 

**==> picture [225 x 178] intentionally omitted <==**

- If the doctor has prescribed any medications in case of an allergic reaction, always keep those medications at hand[ [38]] . 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������� complications caused by food allergies[ [40]] . 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ after a certain amount of time to evaluate whether the child has outgrown the allergy. Some allergies may in fact be outgrown with time, and the foods may end up being tolerated after reaching the age of three or four years old. This must be done under the doctor’s supervision[ [38]] . 

Tips when dining out of the house: 

As a parent of a child with one or more food allergies, eating out of the house can be challenging. The following tips can help you: 

- Check the menu online before going to the restaurant. 

- Read and/or ask about the ingredients before ordering any dish. 

- Let the server be aware of your child’s allergy and ensure there is no cross-contamination when preparing your child’s dish. 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������� 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� dishes[[38]] . 

**==> picture [233 x 178] intentionally omitted <==**

Food allergy card: 

Having a food allergy card can help your child and especially help the people around them (if you ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� child at all times, including at the nursery, when the child is visiting a friend, at a party and/or in a restaurant. Inform any adult in charge that the child has this card, such as the teacher at the nursery or the parents of the friend that your child is visiting [38]. 

The food allergy card should contain the following information: 

- The name of the child 

- Food items your child is allergic to 

- What to do in case of emergency 

- Parent’s name and phone number 

This card can be easily done at home (below is the card template).

## **Food Safety Considerations** 

Complementary feeding (i.e., solid and soft foods) should be introduced at six months of age. Babies have a higher risk of food poisoning due to their immature immune systems. Therefore, it urc sig ecitcarp ot laicooh dyeigna enorp dpof reoh dannilda ot gva dionof fo sesac yop dsioonin .g Keep these simple vital tips in mind to ensure that you and your baby will have a fruitful experience when introducing solid and soft foods[[4]] . 

- Always wash your hands thoroughly before preparing the food and before feeding your baby. 

- Always wash your baby’s hands before feeding as they will uncontrollably want to feed themselves. 

- Always use clean utensils and surfaces when preparing food and when feeding your baby. 

- Always ensure that food is cooked thoroughly. 

- Always store food safely in airtight containers and appropriate temperatures. 

By paying close attention to hygienic practices, you can lower the incidence of gastrointestinal illnesses such as diarrhea. Refer to Appendix 2.

## **Physical Activity Recommendations for Infants and Young Children** 

It is important for the development of your child to have some form of physical activity. This can be achieved in various ways: 

## **For infants (<12 months)[ [44, 45]] :** 

An exercise regimen for infants is impractical: infants do not follow instructions. However, it is crucial to facilitate some form of physical activity daily. 

Interact often with your baby and provide opportunities for “tummy time”. 

- Tummy time is when you place your baby on their stomach while they are awake, and only when supervised. 

- Tummy time can help develop strength in your baby’s neck, arms and back. 

- You can start your baby’s tummy time “training” as soon as you leave the hospital. During ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� 10-15 minutes per day. As your baby grows and gains strength you should extend the time gradually. 

- Initiate tummy time when your baby is energetic following a nap or a diaper change. 

- Create a safe environment such as a playmat or clean towel. You might want to add some toys to stimulate your baby’s attention. 

- Once your baby starts enjoying this position gradually increase the session frequency and duration throughout the day. If your baby is not able to crawl yet, aim for a minimum of 30 minutes per day in several “tummy time” sessions. 

- As good as tummy time is for your baby, never put your baby to sleep on their stomach. ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� (SIDS). 

For a healthy development, avoid “locking up” your child in prams, strollers, or highchairs for more than 60 minutes. Your baby develops daily and needs to start exploring their surroundings. Make sure to allow some opportunities for: 

- Floor-based play. 

- Reaching out and grabbing objects. 

- Crawling. 

## **For toddlers (1-2 years)[[44-46]] :** 

Toddlers this age should engage in at least 3 hours of physical activity throughout the day (not all at once). This should be achieved through fun activities that promote exploration and discovery. Below are some tips for you and your toddler: 

- Include a wider variety of physical activity options through active play (e.g., standing, rolling, playing, and moving around). 

- When the child starts walking, encourage them to walk more, and move around the house. 

- When the child can balance well, encourage them to take part in activities such as running, jumping, climbing, swimming, bouncing, catching, kicking, ball games etc. 

- **�������������������������������������������������������[ [44, 45] ]** 

Physical activity helps infants and toddlers to: 

- Develop locomotor and movement skills 

- Develop strong bones and muscles 

- Maintain a healthy weight 

- Improve social and intellectual skills 

- Adopting physical activity as a habit early in life 

## **Safety tips[[44]] :** 

- Activities should be based on physical maturity rather than chronological age to reduce the risk of injury, because each child grows at their own pace. 

- Frequency, intensity, and time should gradually progress as the child develops. 

- Supervise your child to prevent at home-accidents. 

## **Limiting sedentary behavior (sitting)[[44, 45]] :** 

Reducing sedentary behavior (sitting or restrained) during your child’s waking hours is recommended to support healthy growth and development. 

- Do not allow any screen time for children under the age of two years. 

- Do not restrain your child for more than one hour at a time (i.e., in a highchair or stroller). 

- Integrate active fun activities in the child’s everyday routines. 

- Keep electronic equipment out of sight.

**Make sure to include protein rich foods in your child’s daily diet. These include legumes, �������������������������������������������������������������������** 

General recommendations for protein foods are 2 portions per day. 

## **Examples of one portion include:** 

- 2-4 tablespoons of cooked beans, chickpeas or lentils 

- 15-30 g of seafood, skinless chicken, and lean meats 

- ½-1 ½  tablespoon of canned sardines 

- ½-1 ½ tablespoon of canned tuna (in water not oil) 

- ½-1 boiled egg 

- 1-2 tablespoons of chopped or ground unsalted, raw nuts or seeds 

- 1-2 tablespoons of hummus 

- 1 tablespoon of peanut butter 

The number of portions of protein per day increases with the child’s age: 2 portions/day for toddlers aged 1-2 years; 2-5 portions for children aged 2-5 years. 

## **APPENDIX 2:** 

GENERAL FOOD SAFETY CONSIDERATIONS 

Eating food contaminated with certain bacteria, viruses, parasites or contains harmful toxins can cause foodborne illnesses. These illnesses are usually acute, occurring within 1 to 36 hours after consuming the contaminated or poisonous food. The symptoms typically last from 1 to 7 days and include one or more of the following symptoms: abdominal pain, diarrhea, vomiting, feeling sick, dehydration and collapsing. Foods that are most likely to contain harmful bacteria or viruses fall into two categories: 

1. Uncooked fresh vegetables and fruits 

2. Some animal products, such as unpasteurized (raw) milk; soft cheeses made with raw milk; ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� juices; luncheon meats and deli-type salads (without added preservatives) 

While most children who develop a foodborne illness will get better without medical interventions, it is advisable to consult with the doctor if symptoms are severe or persist for more than a week. 

Preparing and consuming safe foods starts at the time of food purchase. Box 1 outlines a few tips to assist you in shopping for safe food for your children. 

## Box 1. Tips for safe food purchase 

- Purchase food from reliable sources. 

- Read the “Product Label” for food safety information on all foods and beverages. 

- Put raw seafood, poultry, or meat in separate plastic bags. 

- Pick up perishable foods last, and plan to go directly home from the grocery store. 

**==> picture [97 x 97] intentionally omitted <==**

- Buy only pasteurized milk, soft cheeses made with pasteurized milk, and pasteurized juices that have been treated to control harmful bacteria. 

- Always purchase refrigerated eggs. 

- Do not buy food displayed in unsafe or unclean conditions. 

- Always check the expiry date of the food to be purchased: 

   - A “Sell-By” or “Expiry (EXP)” date tells the store how long to display the product for sale. You should buy the product before the date expires. 

   - ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� not a purchase or safety date. 

   - A “Use-By” date is the last date recommended for product use while at peak quality. The date has been determined by the manufacturer of the product. 

����������������������������������������������������������������������������� ensure proper handling and consumption. These practices fall under the following four categories: **Clean, Separate, Cook and Chill** . More details about these practices are outlined in Box 2[ [48]] . Box 2. Tips for proper food handling **Clean:** • Wash your hands before, during, and after food preparation and consumption. • Wash your hands with soap for at least 60 seconds. • Practice good personal hygiene during food handling and preparation activities. • ����������������������������������������������������������������������������� tabletops, cooking surfaces and the sink with hot, soapy water before you cook and after they come into contact with raw seafood, poultry, meat, eggs �������� • ����������������������������������������������������������������������������� Vinegar may also be used to disinfect vegetables and fruits. • Limit washing eggs, raw meat and poultry since washing causes bacteria to spread faster. Instead, pat the eggs with a clean, damp towel and the raw meat and poultry with a separate damp towel as well. • Wipe food packaging with soap and water before opening, especially the lids of cans and jars. 

**==> picture [378 x 258] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
|||
|---|---|
|Separate:|• Keep cooked and ready-to-eat foods away from raw seafood, poultry,|
|meat, and eggs in the refrigerator while cooking. Juices from raw seafood,|
|poultry, meats and cracked eggs can contaminate ready-to-eat foods, so it is|
|important to separate them.|
|• Ensure that cooked and ready-to-eat foods are placed on top shelves, while|
|raw foods are placed on lower shelves in the refrigerator in order to prevent|
|the transfer of bacteria from raw foods to cooked foods.|
|• If possible, use separate sets of knives, cutting boards, and utensils for|
|seafood, poultry, meat, and eggs. Ensure to wash them in hot, soapy water or|
|in the dishwasher between uses.|
|• Plates that touch raw foods are not safe to reuse for cooked foods until they|
|have been washed. Use clean plates to hold cooked foods, and wash plates|
|thoroughly in hot, soapy water after they touch raw foods.|
|56|

**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


- **Cook:** • Use clean water. 

   - Cook all food thoroughly: 

      - The cooking temperature needs to reach at least 75º C or above to ensure the food is safe and free from all pathogenic bacteria. 

      - A food thermometer must be used to measure the internal temperature of cooked foods. Check the internal temperature in several places to make sure that the seafood, poultry, meat, or egg product is cooked to safe minimum internal temperatures. 

      - For microwave or oven cooking: always cover food, stir, and rotate for even cooking. 

   - Consume leftovers within 3-4 days. 

   - Reheat leftovers only once. If leftovers are not consumed after being reheated, throw them out. 

## **Chill:** 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������� �������������������������������������������������������������������������� bacteria. 

- Do not keep food at room temperature for more than 2 hours. 

There are a few general guidelines that will help reduce the risk of foodborne illnesses: 

- Protect food from insects, rodents, and other animals. 

- Store non-perishable food products in a cool and dry place. 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� fruit juice. 

- You cannot tell by looking, smelling, or even tasting a food whether it contains pathogens. Yet these pathogens-like disease causing bacteria, viruses, or parasites, can make you sick. 

- You should never taste food to determine if it is safe to eat.

Healthy diets are important at every age. This chapter focuses on toddlers aged 2-3 years and preschoolers aged 3-5 years. Toddlers and preschoolers are very receptive and impressionable, which gives you the perfect opportunity to help them establish healthy eating habits. Although toddlers and preschoolers have a slower growth compared to infants, they still need enough energy to fuel their active play and enough nutrients to support their growth and development. 

**==> picture [311 x 53] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
01<br>Assessment of Child’s Weight and Height<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


It is important that a doctor or healthcare provider monitors the growth of your child by measuring his/her weight, height, and head circumference (for children under 24-36 months). The doctor will later draw these measurements on the appropriate growth charts in order to assess your child’s growth and development. 

## **What are growth charts?** 

- Growth charts are graphic presentations that illustrate the distribution of body measurements in children (weight, height, head circumference, body mass index (BMI)). 

- Growth charts are the most useful tool for assessing growth and nutritional status in children. 

- The use of the appropriate growth charts may identify abnormal trends in growth that can be indicative of poor nutrition or the presence of disease. 

In some instances, the measurements may reveal certain growth-related problems, such as: 

- The child has a low weight for his/her age (underweight or severely underweight): This may be the result of the child being too thin or too short for his/her age. It may be the result of poor nutrition or certain illnesses. Underweight children are more vulnerable to diseases and may experience delays in their development. 

- The child is short for his/her age (stunted or severely stunted): If your child’s height is below the normal range for his/her age (a condition referred to as stunting), this may be the result of long-term malnutrition or illness. It has consequences on the physical development of the child and is often accompanied by poor mental development. 

- The child has lost weight (wasted or severely wasted): This may occur because of poor nutrition or illness. Wasted children have a higher risk of contracting diseases and illnesses. 

**==> picture [133 x 133] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [151 x 151] intentionally omitted <==**

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� genetic factors (i.e., running in the family), or a combination of all these factors. In rare cases, obesity in children may result from a medical condition, which is diagnosed by the doctor. Overweight and obesity early in life can increase the risk of obesity and chronic diseases later in life. 

- The child has a larger-than-normal or smaller-than-normal head circumference: This helps in assessing brain size as an indicator of possible developmental or nutritional problems. 

Box 1 below summarizes the health and social implications associated with overweight and obesity, as well as those associated with the child being underweight, wasted, or stunted[ [1, 2]] . 

Box 1. Implications associated with overweight and obesity, as well as those associated with underweight, wasting, and stunting among 2–5-year-old children 

**Overweight and obesity** 

- Social problems including bullying 

- ��������������������������������������������������� 

- Lower quality of life 

- Type 2 diabetes, high blood pressure, high blood cholesterol, and cardiovascular diseases later in life 

- Joints and bone problems 

**Underweight, wasting, and stunting** 

- Social problems including bullying 

- Delayed mental growth and reduced intellectual capacity 

- Poor school performance 

- Increased risk of infections and illness

03 Fluid Intake Recommendations<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ recommendations according to your child’s age[ [6]] : 

- **2–3-year-old:** 4 cups (1 L) from water (and other beverages). 

- **4–5-year-old:** 5 cups (1.25 L) from water (and other beverages). 

- 1 cup = 250 mL 

If you were told by a doctor that your child is underweight or obese, then make sure to consult ������������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

When choosing beverages other than water, be aware that: 

- Sugar-sweetened beverages such as carbonated soft drinks and fruit drinks should be limited. These are high in added sugars, which can contribute to tooth decay and weight gain, while also replacing other more nutritious beverages such as milk. 

- Fruits are rich in natural sugars. Hence, fresh fruit juices are high in nutrients but are also ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� maximum of one serving (125 mL- half a cup) of fresh fruit juice (with no added sugar) to your child per day.

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
04<br>How to Boost My Child’s Immunity<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


Children need adequate intakes of nutrients and vitamins to help boost their immune system and protect them against infections. However, there are no magical foods or supplements that will boost your child’s immune system[[7]] . The best advice for supporting your child’s immunity is ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� diet that is varied and balanced which consists of food and beverages from the six food groups. Prioritize foods that are nutrient-rich such as vegetables and fruits which supply an abundant amount of antioxidants, vitamins, and minerals. Make sure to also limit their consumption of processed foods, snacks and foods that are high in sugar, salt, and unhealthy fats. Review Appendix 1 for details pertinent to dietary recommendations for your child.

## **05 Picky Eating** 

Many children go through a phase of refusing certain food types, especially when trying new foods. These children are known as “picky eaters”. This behavior tends to occur especially in ����������������������������������������������������������������������������[[8, 9]] . It is the child’s way of showing you their independence; it is also considered a normal phase of growing up. If ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� stressful. But you need to know that picky eating rarely causes any serious nutritional, medical or growth problems for the child, and it is a phase that most children grow out of it[[8]] . 

�������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� eaters.” In these cases, professionals may consider this as a feeding disorder, and you will need the help of a health professional to help your child grow out of it. The section below explains the �������������������������������������������������������[ [8]] . 

## **Picky eaters & Extreme picky eaters** 

Extreme picky eating can last for a longer time as compared to picky eating. Extreme picky eaters can grow out of it over months or years; however, this usually needs to be done with the help of a health professional[[8]] . Extreme picky eating is usually more common in children with social communication disorders[[8]] . 

Although being a picky eater usually is harmless, being an extreme picky eater can cause serious ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[[8]] . Table 2 provides you with a direct comparison between the two behaviors.

## **When to seek professional help?** 

Do not get frustrated if your child is a picky eater. Just provide your child with healthy food choices and try your best to help your child grow out of this phase. In fact, most picky eaters remain healthy, and their eating habits tend to improve gradually as they get older[[10]] . If your ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� this problem[[8]] .

- Encourage good behavior at mealtime by rewarding the child with “non-food” items. 

- Verbal praise or a loving look are considered positive in developing food preferences.

## **Force-Feeding** 

Mothers tend to get worried when their child eats very little, refuses to eat a meal or refuses to eat healthy foods like fruits and vegetables[[11]] �������������������������������������������������� especially if the child is underweight or not gaining weight adequately. For others, unconsumed meals can be a source of frustration, especially when the parents do not like to waste food that has been prepared, or when they believe that children have to ‘clean their plates’[[11]] .  As a result, parents may end up forcing their child to eat their entire meal. 

It is true that the child may end up eating a bit more when being forced to eat. However, studies have shown that the act of forcing the child to eat can cause long-term problems for the child, which are summarized below: 

- **Disliking or avoiding certain foods.** This can be the result of a negative experience of ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� between foods and unpleasant experiences that may accompany them[ [11]] . 

- **Disturbing the child’s ability to respond to their internal feelings of hunger and fullness.** This means that the child would not listen to his/her body and so food intake becomes determined by other factors other than what the body requires. Instead, the child learns to continue eating, even when they feel full, stopping only when the plate is empty[ [11]] . 

- **Development of overeating and overweight.** As explained above, forcing the child to eat can disturb the child’s ability to learn appropriate appetite control. This can eventually lead to overeating and the development of overweight and obesity[ [11]] . 

Except in rare cases, children are usually extremely good at knowing when they are full, and ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� that they will eat when feeling hungry. It is also important to remember that children have a natural tendency to reject new foods and this should not be met with pressure. Instead, continue ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� development. Also remember that the stomachs of young children are smaller than adults’ and you may be serving too much food that your child cannot consume. 

**==> picture [182 x 53] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
07<br>Vegetarian Children<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


Some families will choose to limit meat consumption or follow a vegetarian diet for health or �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� based foods (such as vegetables, fruits, cereals and starchy vegetables, legumes, unsalted, raw nuts and seeds), and usually excludes some or all foods from the animal-based food items such ������������������������������������������������������� 

If you choose this dietary pattern for your child, you should consult with a doctor or dietitian ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ suggests that, if done properly, and if monitored by a healthcare provider, vegetarian diets can meet the nutrient requirements of young children[[12-14]] .

## **08 Tips for A Healthy and Safe Lunchbox** 

**==> picture [115 x 109] intentionally omitted <==**

Since foodborne illness are very common if foods are not properly stored in the lunchbox, or consumed at the right temperature, you need to follow some safety guidelines[[15]] : 

- For foods that should be kept cold, you might need to use an insulated bag with some sort �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� reusable cold source by simply adding a frozen water bottle or container to the lunchbox. 

- Avoid giving your child hot meals especially if the daycare/school does not have the option of heating foods. Remember that meals should be heated up to a safe temperature before being consumed. 

For a healthy child’s lunchbox, follow the below guidelines (Box 3)[[16]] . 

|Box 3. Guidelines to follow when preparing your child’s lunchbox|Box 3. Guidelines to follow when preparing your child’s lunchbox|Box 3. Guidelines to follow when preparing your child’s lunchbox|
|---|---|---|
|**Choices**|•|Fill the lunchbox as such:|
|||• ������������������������������������������������������|
|||• ¼ of it with whole grain cereals|
|||• ¼ of it with healthy proteins (legumes, turkey breast, unsalted, raw nuts/seeds)|
||•|Add milk and/or dairy products to the main meal or snacks (such as a 200 mL pack|
|||of pasteurized milk).|
|**Preparation**|•|Make sure that the vegetables and fruits are thoroughly washed.|
||•|Involve your child in the lunchbox preparation such as washing the vegetables and|
|||��������������������������������������������������������������������|
|||meal combination.|



- **Presentation** • Cut the vegetables and fruits into small cubes or pieces, rather than putting them as whole food items. 

- • ���������������������������������������������������������� 

      - Green theme: Add lettuce, cucumbers as vegetables / apples, pears as fruits; 

   - Red theme: Add cubes of a red tomato, slices of red pepper, raspberries, and strawberries. 

   - • Incorporate more shapes: Present the sandwiches as small squares, or in the form of triangles; Use the dough-shaped cutters to cut the vegetables or fruits into nice shapes. 

- **Snack ideas** • Pair protein-rich foods with carbohydrate-rich foods: • 1 cup of plain yogurt with ½ a cup of strawberries or blueberries • 1 slice of whole wheat bread with peanut butter spread (1 tablespoon) • Carrot sticks with hummus dip • Cucumber cubes or slices with ½ a cup of labneh dip • 1 cup of seedless grapes with slices of white cheese 

- **Water** • Do not forget your child’s water bottle!

## **10** 

## **Food Allergies** 

�����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[[17]] . �����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [17, ] 18]. The majority of children who have milk, egg, wheat or soy allergies would outgrow these ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� usually lifelong[ [17, 19]] . 

Food allergy is not the same as food intolerance, although the two terms are often mixed up. ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� immune system, whereas food allergies cause an immune system reaction[[17]] . The symptoms of food intolerance are usually less serious and are often limited to digestive problems. In contrast, ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� that can vary in their degree of severity. In some cases, allergic reactions may be very severe and life-threatening. 

## **What are the most common allergens in the diet?** 

����������������������������������������������������������������������������[[17, 20]] : 

- Animal-based milk such as cow’s milk 

- Eggs 

- Peanuts 

- Soy 

- Tree nuts 

- Fish 

- ����������������������������������� 

- Wheat 

**==> picture [172 x 86] intentionally omitted <==**

- Seeds 

����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� type of food from your child’s diet[[20]] . 

Some individuals can have allergies for food additives including colors and preservatives, but usually allergic reactions from ordinary food items are more common[ [20]] . 

**==> picture [65 x 62] intentionally omitted <==**

## **What are the symptoms of food allergies?** 

An allergic reaction can begin within minutes to an hour after ingesting the food or beverage that �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� more symptoms. The most common symptoms of food allergy are[[17]] : 

- Diarrhea 

- Vomiting 

- Cough 

- Swelling 

- Dry and itchy skin (eczema) 

- Itching or swelling of the lips, tongue, or mouth 

- Itching or tightness in the throat 

- Skin rashes 

- Sore, red and/or itchy eyes 

- Runny or blocked nose 

**==> picture [118 x 118] intentionally omitted <==**

- Lowered blood pressure 

- Stomach cramps and pain 

- Red itchy bumps on the skin (hives) 

- Trouble breathing or shortness of breath 

- Wheezing (coarse sound when breathing) 

In some cases, severe allergic reaction may occur which is known as “anaphylaxis”; this can be life-threating[[20,21]] ������������������������������������������������������������������������������ ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[[17]] . 

## **How do we diagnose a food allergy?** 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ unnecessary dietary restrictions. In case a food allergy is diagnosed, you must have a dietary plan to replace the eliminated food items, and you also need to have a plan in case of emergency[[19]] . If your child develops any of the typical allergy-related symptoms after eating any type of food or beverage, you should immediately contact a doctor. 

**==> picture [130 x 129] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Nutritional concerns in children with food allergies** 

It is important to keep in mind that eliminating a certain food group (because of an allergy) ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� problems in your child[ [22]] . For example, milk, eggs and soy are good sources of fat and protein. ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� protein and fat in the diet if they are not replaced by other good sources[[22]] . 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� energy (calories) and certain vitamins, which can lead to poor growth. 

- Diets that are low in protein may also lead to protein malnutrition and hence poor growth [22]. 

Another example is wheat. This cereal provides the body with carbohydrates, which are known to be an important source of energy for your child’s body, and particularly the brain. Wheat also contains important vitamins and minerals. So if the child is allergic to wheat, other alternative �����������������������������������������������������������������������������[[22]] . 

Another potential challenge is that children that have one or more food allergies might experience some dietary behavior problems more than other children. For example, they may develop “food aversion” (i.e. refusing certain types of food) or a state of anxiety about food, which again can lead to inadequate food intake[[22]] . 

This is why it is very important that the doctor monitors the growth of children with food allergies [22]. It is also important that the doctor or dietitians provide you with the right alternatives to ����������������������������������������������������������������������[ [22]] .  Supplements may sometimes be prescribed by the doctor when needed[[22]] . 

## **What should I do if my child was diagnosed with a food allergy?** 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ food or beverage that causes the allergic reaction[[17, 19, 21, 23]] . It is therefore important to get the help of a dietitian to plan an adequate, healthy and balanced diet for your child, to avoid any �������������������������������������������������������������������������������[[23]] . Below are some practical tips that can help you in managing your child’s food allergy: 

- Check with a dietitian and a doctor to identify food alternatives or even nutritional �������������������������������������[[17]] . 

**==> picture [124 x 128] intentionally omitted <==**

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������[[19]] . 

- Educate your family (at home) and teachers (in the school or nursery) about your child’s allergies and what to do in case of an emergency[[19]] . 

- If the doctor has prescribed any medications in case of an allergic reaction, always keep those medications at hand[[17]] . 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������� complications caused by food allergies[ [21]] . 

���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� allergies, after a certain amount of time to evaluate whether the child has outgrown the allergy. Some allergies may in fact be outgrown with time and the foods may end up being tolerated after reaching the age of three or four years old. This must be done under the doctor’s supervision[[17]] . 

## **Tips when dining out of the house:** 

As a parent of a child with one or more food allergies, it can be challenging to eat out of the house. The following tips can help you: 

- Check the menu online before going to the restaurant. 

- Read and/or ask about the ingredients before ordering any dish. 

- Let the server be aware of your child’s allergy and ensure there is no cross-contamination when preparing your child’s dish. 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������� 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� dishes[[17]] . 

## **Food allergy card:** 

Having a food allergy card can help your child and especially help the people around them (if you ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� with the child at all times, including at the school or nursery, or when the child is visiting a friend, at a party and/or in a restaurant. Inform any adult in charge that the child has this card, such as the teacher at the school or nursery the parents of the friend that your child is visiting[ [17]] . 

The food allergy card should contain the following information: 

- The name of the child 

- Food items your child is allergic to 

- What to do in case of emergency 

- Parent’s name and phone number 

This card can be easily done at home (below is the card template).

11 Oral Health<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


Proper oral health among children paves the way for good health and wellbeing as they grow older. Early childhood is the most convenient time for your child to acquire healthy habits since at this age, they would have started to drink and eat on their own. Unhealthy diets and improper oral health habits may increase your child’s risk of dental decays, especially if your child engages in the following behaviors[[24]] : 

- Regular and frequent consumption of sugary foods like cakes, biscuits,  candies, and chocolates 

- Regular and frequent consumption of sugar-sweetened beverages like fruit juices and carbonated soft drinks (i.e., carbonated beverages) 

- Not cleaning or brushing their teeth 

Hence, it is extremely important that you consider the below recommendations to ensure adequate oral health for your child (Box 4)[ [24]] . 

Box 4. Recommendations to ensure adequate oral health for your child 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� such as vegetables, fruits, and yogurt. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ ������������������� 

- Watch your child brush their teeth and help them until they have acquired good brushing techniques. 

- Try to make teeth brushing fun by using a timer (2 minutes). Let them use a toothbrush with an animated character that they like; this will motivate them to brush their teeth. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� recommendation. 

- Ensure your child is having regular dental check-ups with a dentist (at least every 6 months).

## **Your Child’s Food Choices** 

Every parent tries their best to ensure that their child eats healthy most of the time, but there [25]. 

Food and beverage options that are advertised in the media (TV or social media) are not always nutritious or healthy for your child. In fact, most of the advertised food and beverages are high [26]. Children have a remarkable ability to remember content from these advertisements and thus they tend to develop a preference for the marketed foods[[25, 27-29]] . 

## **choices?[[26]]** 

- Avoid the use of TVs and tablets or any other electronic device while eating: 

   - Apply this to the whole family during main meals as well as snacks. 

   - Eat together as a family without any distractions to promote healthy eating as well as family bonding. 

- Choose children’s programs without advertisements: 

   - Choose platforms that allow you to skip commercials, or that do not include any. 

- Involve your child when buying and preparing foods: 

   - Children are willing to learn about everything at this age, and they enjoy being involved in doing small tasks around the house; this is a good opportunity to teach them about healthy food and beverages and let them be part of choosing, buying, and preparing meals and snacks. 

- Limit screen time: 

   - Limit screen time to a maximum of one hour per day. 

- Be a role model to your child: 

   - Young children will imitate their parents and view them as their role models. Be mindful of your choices. Choose healthy foods and beverages and limit your screen time to encourage your child to do the same. 

**==> picture [122 x 121] intentionally omitted <==**

## **13 Physical Activity Recommendations For Toddlers and Preschoolers** 

Encourage your child to lead a healthy and active lifestyle by being involved in unstructured or structured play for a minimum of 3 hours a day[[30]] . 

��������������������������������������������������������������������������[ [30]] : 

- It promotes healthy and strong bones and muscles, while improving movement skills 

- It helps maintain a healthy body weight 

- It improves social and intellectual skills 

Box 5 below provides you with the physical activity recommendations for toddlers and preschoolers [30]. 

## Box 5. Physical activity guidelines for toddlers and preschoolers 

- Encourage your child to enjoy a variety of activities throughout the day, such as riding the bicycle, running, jumping, and swimming. 

- Make sure to use protective gear such as bicycle helmets, knee pads and chin guards, to help reduce the risk of injuries. 

- Gradually increase the frequency, time, and intensity of exercising as your child is growing and developing. 

- Limit long hours of inactivity by encouraging your child to move more and by making physical activity part of their daily routine. Encourage a break from sitting, every 20-30 minutes. 

- Limit screen time (television, computer, phones, tablets) to less than an hour per day. 

**==> picture [143 x 143] intentionally omitted <==**

Every child is ������������������������� activities should be based on their current physical maturity. Gradually increase frequency, intensity, and time of new physical activities to reduce **REMEMBER** the risk of injury. Accidents happen more frequently when your child gets tired or due to missing protective gear.

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
14 Importance of Adequate Sleep<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


Adequate sleep plays a major role in modulating the health and wellbeing of your child. ������������������������������������������������������������������������������[[31, 32]] , and can increase the risk of developing chronic diseases, such as hypertension, cardiovascular diseases and type II diabetes later in life[[32, 33]] . In addition, lack of sleep can have a negative impact on the following[ [33, 34]] : 

- Physical and mental health 

- Cognitive and psychosocial development 

- Alertness and attention 

- Vocabulary acquisition (process of learning new words) 

- Learning and memory 

- Mood 

Box 6 provides you with the recommendations for sleep among toddlers and preschoolers[ [32, 33, 35]] . 

## Box 6. Recommendations for sleep among toddlers and preschoolers 

- Make sure that your child is getting good quality of sleep as follows: 

   - 11-14 hours of sleep, including naps, for children aged 2-3 years old. 

   - 10-13 hours of sleep, including naps, for children aged 3-5 years old. Naps at this age become shorter; preschoolers might even stop napping. 

- Establish a consistent bedtime routine. Reading a book, or having a hot warm bath can help. 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� bedtime. Let the bed be a no-screen zone. 

- Make sure that the bedroom is quiet, calm and at a room temperature convenient for your child. 

- Having your child put on their favorite pajamas is a good strategy to encourage them to go to bed. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ 

- Encourage your child to have a proper physical activity routine, which can help them sleep better at night. Refer to section 13. 

**==> picture [125 x 121] intentionally omitted <==**

- Do not forget proper teeth brushing before bedtime! (Refer to Section 11).

Box 1:  Protein Foods<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


**Make sure to include protein rich foods in your child’s daily diet. These include legumes, �������������������������������������������������������������������** 

General recommendations for protein foods are 2 portions per day. 

## **Examples of one portion include:** 

- 2-4 tablespoons of cooked beans, chickpeas or lentils 

- 15-30 g of seafood, skinless chicken, and lean meats 

- ½-1 ½  tablespoon of canned sardines 

- ½-1 ½ tablespoon of canned tuna (in water not oil) 

- ½-1 boiled egg 

- 1-2 tablespoons of chopped or ground unsalted, raw nuts or seeds 

- 1-2 tablespoons of hummus 

- 1 tablespoon of peanut butter 

The number of portions of protein per day increases with the child’s age: 2 portions/day for toddlers aged 1-2 years; 2-5 portions for children aged 2-5 years. 

## **APPENDIX 2:** 

���������������������������������� 

Eating food that is contaminated with certain bacteria, viruses, parasites or contains harmful toxins can cause foodborne illnesses. These illnesses are usually acute, occurring within 1 to 36 hours after the consumption of the contaminated or poisonous food. The symptoms normally last from 1 to 7 days and include one or more of the following symptoms: abdominal pain, diarrhea, vomiting, feeling sick, dehydration and collapsing. Foods that are most likely to contain harmful bacteria or viruses fall into two categories: 

1. Uncooked fresh vegetables and fruits 

2. Some animal products, such as unpasteurized (raw) milk; soft cheeses made with raw milk; ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� juices; luncheon meats and deli-type salads (without added preservatives) 

While the majority of children who develop a foodborne illness will get better without medical interventions, if symptoms are severe or persist for more than a week, it is advisable to consult with a doctor. 

Preparing and consuming safe foods starts at the time of food purchase. Box 1 outlines a few tips to assist you in shopping for safe food for your children. 

**==> picture [162 x 162] intentionally omitted <==**

Box 1. Tips for safe food purchase 

- Purchase food from reliable sources. 

- Read the “Product Label” for food safety information on all foods and beverages. 

- Put raw seafood, poultry, or meat in separate plastic bags. 

- Pick up perishable foods last, and plan to go directly home from the grocery store. 

- Buy only pasteurized milk, soft cheeses made with pasteurized milk, and pasteurized juices that have been treated to control harmful bacteria. 

- Always purchase refrigerated eggs. 

- Do not buy food displayed in unsafe or unclean conditions. 

- Always check the expiry date of the food to be purchased: 

   - A “Sell-By” or “Expiry (EXP)” date tells the store how long to display the product for ��������������������������������������������������������� 

   - �� �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� not a purchase or safety date. 

   - A “Use-By” date is the last date recommended for the use of the product while at peak quality. The date has been determined by the manufacturer of the product. 

������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� handling and consumption. These practices fall under the following four categories: **Clean, Separate, Cook and Chill** . More details about these practices are outlined in Box 2[[37]] . 

**==> picture [159 x 159] intentionally omitted <==**

|Box 2. Tips for proper food handling|Box 2. Tips for proper food handling|
|---|---|
|**Clean:**|• Wash your hands, before, during and after food preparation and|
||consumption.|
||• Wash your hands for at least 60 seconds.|
||• Practice good personal hygiene during food handling and preparation|
||activities.|
||• Clean your kitchen! Keep all food preparation premises clean; wash|
||counters, tabletops, cooking surfaces and the sink with hot, soapy water|
||before you cook and after they come into contact with raw seafood,|
||������������������������|
||• Clean your food! Wash vegetables and fruits with clean water, before|
||peeling. Vinegar may also be used to disinfect vegetables and fruits.|
||• Limit washing eggs, raw meat and poultry since washing causes bacteria|
||to spread faster. Instead, pat the eggs with a clean, damp towel, and the|
||raw meat and poultry with a separate damp towel as well.|
||• Wipe food packaging with soap and water before opening, especially lids|
||of cans and jars.|
|**Separate:**|• Keep cooked and ready-to-eat foods away from raw seafood, poultry,|
||meat, and eggs in the refrigerator and while cooking. (Juices from raw|
||seafood, poultry, meats and cracked eggs can contaminate ready-to-eat|
||foods, so it is important to separate them.)|
||• Ensure that cooked and ready-to-eat foods are placed on top shelves,|
||while raw foods are placed on lower shelves in the refrigerator, in order to|
||prevent the transfer of bacteria from the raw foods to the cooked foods.|
||• If possible, use separate sets of knives, cutting boards, and utensils for|
||seafood, poultry, meat, and eggs. Ensure to wash them in hot, soapy|
||water or in the dishwasher between uses.|
||• Plates that touch raw foods are not safe to reuse for cooked foods until|
||they have been washed. Use clean plates to hold cooked foods, and wash|
||plates thoroughly in hot, soapy water after they touch raw foods.|



**==> picture [154 x 144] intentionally omitted <==**

- **Cook:** • Use clean water. • Cook all food thoroughly: 

      - The cooking temperature needs to reach at least 75º C or above to ensure the food is safe and free from all pathogenic bacteria. 

      - A food thermometer must be used to measure the internal temperature of cooked foods. Check the internal temperature in several places to make sure that the seafood, poultry, meat, or egg product is cooked to safe minimum internal temperatures. 

      - For microwave or oven cooking: always cover food, stir, and rotate for even cooking. 

   - Consume leftovers within 3-4 days. 

   - Reheat leftovers only once. If leftovers are not consumed after being reheated, throw them out. 

- **Chill:** • ���������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������ harmful bacteria. 

- • Do not keep food at room temperature for more than 2 hours. 

There are a few general guidelines that will help reduce the risk of foodborne illnesses: 

- Protect food from insects, rodents, and other animals. 

- Store non-perishable food products in a cool and dry place. 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� fruit juice. 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������

## **Choose Healthy Fats and Limit Your Child’s Intake of Sugar and Salt** 

Your child’s meals and snacks at home as well as their lunchbox should include nutritious food ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� Dietary Guidelines[[1]] . This means that you need to limit foods that are high in sugar, salt, and unhealthy fats in your child’s diet. 

Many children consume excessive amounts of added sugar from sweetened foods and beverages, which can lead to dental caries and increase their risk for overweight and obesity[ [2, 3]] . Excessive intakes of salt in children may also increase their predisposition to develop hypertension later in life[ [4]] . While infants and toddlers need a higher fat intake compared to older children or adults, it is important that they consume healthy types of fats and oils, and reduce their intake of saturated fat, and hydrogenated and trans-fat. This chapter provides you with information and practical tips on how to choose healthy fats for your child and reduce their intake of added sugar and salt. 

**==> picture [185 x 185] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [47 x 105] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [289 x 53] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
02<br>Limit Sweetened Foods and Beverages<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


While sugars can be naturally occurring in certain foods (such as fruits, fruit juices, milk and dairy products), they can also be added to food during processing[[5]] . Consuming excessive amounts of added sugars adds calories with no nutritional value. In fact, excess intakes have been associated with increased risk of weight gain, high triglycerides levels, insulin resistance, cardiovascular diseases and dental caries, while also being linked with reduced bone strength[[2, 3]] . Their intake should therefore be reduced to a maximum of 10% of your child’s energy intake[[5-7]] . 

Box 1 provides you with some practical tips to limit your child’s intake of sweetened foods and beverages[ [1, 3, 8]] . 

## Box 1. Practical tips to limit the intake of sweetened foods and beverages 

- Provide your child with three main meals and two nutritious snacks to avoid temptations to eat high sugar foods due to hunger. 

- Encourage your child to snack on fresh vegetables, fruits, dates, and yogurt. 

- Restrict your child’s consumption of carbonated soft drinks, carbonated and sugar-sweetened beverages. 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ or fresh fruit juices (in moderation – ½ a cup per day). 

- If your child is reluctant to accept regular milk, blend fresh fruits or dates with the milk. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� Eastern sweets (such as basboosah and baklava) as well as cakes, desserts, chocolates and confectioneries (candies, lollipops, chewing gum, and jellies). 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� child, make sure to prepare them  with low sugar content (and low-fat milk for children aged above two years) (small portions or lesser amounts). 

- Consider using natural sources of sugar such as dates or apple sauce when preparing desserts. 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� instead of sugar or chocolate-coated cereals. 

**==> picture [123 x 101] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Nutrition labeling:** 

- When choosing packaged foods, check the list of ingredients and make sure sugar is towards the end of the list, since ingredients are listed in order of decreasing weight. 

- When reading nutrition labels, you might also come across the following terms that indicate the presence of sugar: added sugar, brown sugar, glucose, sucrose, fructose, corn sweetener, corn syrup, high fructose corn syrup, honey, dextrose, fruit juice concentrates, invert sugar, malt sugar, molasses, raw sugar and ingredients ending in “-ose.” This usually indicate that this product contains sugar. 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������� 

   - High: contains more than 22.5g of total sugars per 100g of food. 

   - Medium: contains more than 5g and up to 22.5g of total sugars per 100g of food. 

   - Low: contains 5g or less of total sugars per 100g of food. 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������� 

   - High: contains more than 11.25g of total sugars per 100mL. 

   - Medium: contains more than 2.5g and up to 11.25g of total sugars per 100mL. 

   - Low: contains less than 2.5g of total sugars per 100mL. 

- Refer to section 5 below for more information on nutrition labels. 

**==> picture [156 x 156] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [36 x 53] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
03<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## **Reduce Intake of Table Salt and Salty Foods and Beverages** 

Salt is made of sodium chloride. While sodium is needed for some basic bodily functions[ [5, 9]] , ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� increase blood pressure levels. This increases the risk of having strokes, heart diseases and kidney problems[ [10]] . The World Health Organization (WHO) recommends a reduction of salt intake to less than 5g a day (i.e., 1 teaspoon from all sources) for children aged two years and older[ [11]] . 

Box 2 below presents practical tips to reduce the intake of salt and salty foods and beverages [5, 8, 9]. 

## Box 2. Practical tips to reduce the intake of salt and salty foods and beverages 

- Reduce your child’s consumption of salty foods (fast foods, processed meats such as sausages and salami, processed and spreadable cheeses, sauces high in salt, chips; salty crackers, pretzels, salted popcorn, salted nuts) and beverages such as laban ayran. 

- Limit your child’s intake of pickled foods (pickled vegetables such as turnips, cucumbers, and carrots). 

- Reduce the purchase or preparation of pastries made with salty cheeses (manakeesh, fatayer, sambousa). 

- Make sure that the breads and breakfast cereals your child consumes are not high in salt. 

- Reduce the amount of salt used when cooking and preparing food for your child. Taste the food before adding any salt. 

- ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� based pasta sauces) from the dining table. 

- Purchase low-salt versions of sauces (such as low-salt soy sauce and ketchup). 

- Use more lemon, spices, pepper, herbs, ginger, vinegar, rosemary, garlic, and onion to enhance the ������������������������������������� 

- Soak high-salt white cheeses, such as halloumi and akkawi, in water to remove the excess salt, ���������������������������������� 

- When using canned vegetables, make sure to rinse in water to lower their salt content. 

- Ensure your child eats more homemade meals and dishes, while reducing the intake of fast foods and highly processed foods. 

- Prepare homemade soups instead of purchasing prepacked soups as they are high in salt. 

- Encourage your child to consume unsalted, raw nuts and seeds. 

**==> picture [112 x 112] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Reading nutrition labels:** 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������ 

   - High: contains more than 1.5g of salt (or 600mg of sodium) per 100g of food. 

   - Medium: contains more than 0.3g and up to 1.5g of salt (120mg - 600 mg of sodium) per 100g of food. 

   - Low: contains 0.3g or less of salt (120 mg of sodium) per 100 g of food. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������� 

   - High: contains more than 0.75g of salt (300mg of sodium) per 100 mL. 

   - Medium: contains more than 0.3g and up to 0.75g of salt (120mg – 300mg of sodium) per 100mL. 

   - Low: contains 0.3g or less of salt (120mg of sodium) per 100mL. 

- Refer to section 5 below for more information on nutrition labels. 

**==> picture [324 x 221] intentionally omitted <==**

## **04 Choose Healthy Fats and Oils, While Limiting your Child’s Intake of Saturated Fat and Avoiding Trans-Fat** 

Healthy fats are needed for proper growth and development of infants and young children[ [5, 12]] . ��������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� child and can increase their risk of developing chronic diseases later in life[ [5]] . 

**Low-fat diets are NOT recommended for children under the age of two years![[1, 13]]** Low-fat diets are not appropriate for young children, particularly those under two years, because they are still in their growing phase. Unless the child has an allergy, full-fat milk, yogurt and cheese should be given to children until they are two years old. 

**==> picture [196 x 196] intentionally omitted <==**

Box 3 below presents practical tips to choose healthy fats and oils, while reducing saturated fat ������������������������������������[ [5, 8, 9, 13, 14]] . 

## Box 3. Practical tips to choose healthy fats and oils 

- Encourage your child to consume healthy fats from olives, avocados, tahini, unsalted, raw nuts ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� sardines and light canned tuna). 

- Limit your child’s consumption of saturated fats which is primarily found in fatty meat, poultry skin, cold cuts (sausages, salami), processed meats (hotdog, luncheon meats), full-fat dairy products, yellow cheeses, cream, butter, and tropical oils (coconut and palm oils). 

- Limit the use of butter, cream, ghee, and high-fat sauces (mayonnaise, salad dressings) when cooking and preparing food for your child. Instead, use healthy vegetable oils such as olive, canola, ������������������������������������� 

- Restrict your child’s consumption of foods that contain hydrogenated and trans-fats. These include margarine, shortening, commercially processed baked goods (pastries, crackers, biscuits, pies, and cakes), fried and fast foods (French fries, burgers, shawarma and deep-fried falafel), as well as packaged foods made with hydrogenated oils. 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� Eastern sweets (such as basboosah and baklava) that are high in fat. These sweets can be enjoyed on special occasions. 

- Encourage your child to enjoy more homemade baked goods. 

- �������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� addition to low-fat versions of milk, yogurt and laban, since the full-fat versions are high in saturated fat (for children aged above two years). 

- ����������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� processed and spreadable cheeses. 

- Prepare your child’s foods by steaming, baking, grilling, or sautéing, rather than frying or deepfrying. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� chicken or other poultry, make sure to remove the skin before cooking. 

- Limit your child’s intake of fast-food. 

- Save high-fat and high caloric foods and desserts for special occasions only and in small portions. 

**==> picture [47 x 46] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [133 x 134] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Reading nutrition labels:** 

- When reading the ingredients list, avoid purchasing food products that have the following ingredients: hydrogenated oils or partially hydrogenated oils. 

- Choose products that do not contain trans-fat. 

- ������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

   - High: contains more than 5g of saturated fat per 100g of food. 

   - Medium: contains more than 1.5g and up to 5g of saturated fat per 100g of food. 

   - Low: contains 1.5g or less of saturated fat per 100g of food. 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������� 

   - High: contains more than 2.5g of saturated fat per 100mL. 

   - Medium: contains more than 0.75g and up to 2.5g of saturated fat per 100mL. 

   - Low: contains less than 0.75g of saturated fat per 100mL. 

- Refer to section 5 for more information on nutrition labels. 

**==> picture [47 x 46] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [201 x 200] intentionally omitted <==**

**==> picture [165 x 53] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
05<br>Nutrition Labeling<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


A nutrition label is a tool that will help you make informed decisions about prepackaged foods and beverages before buying them for your child. Box 4 below provides you with tips to familiarize yourself with nutrition labels[[8, 15, 16]] . 

Box 4. Tips to familiarize yourself with nutrition labels 

## **Familiarize yourself with the below terms:** 

Nutrition labels usually include the below components: 

- **Servings per container:** total number of servings in the entire food package or container. Keep in mind that the food product may contain more than one serving. 

- **Calories:** amount of energy provided by one serving of this food or beverage. 

- **Nutrients:** total fats (saturated fats and trans-fats), cholesterol, sodium, total carbohydrates ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� calcium, iron, and potassium). 

**==> picture [199 x 200] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Keep in mind the following: For Food:** 

- Aim for less than 5g of sugar per 100g of food. 

- Aim for less than 0.3g of salt per 100g of food. 

- Aim for less than 3g of total fat per 100g of food. 

- Aim for less than 1.5g of saturated fat per 100g of food. 

- Aim for less than 0.2g of trans-fat per 100g of food. 

## **For Beverages:** 

- Aim for less than 2.5g of sugar per 100mL of a beverage. 

- Aim for less than 0.3g of salt per 100mL of a beverage. 

- Aim for less than 1.5g of total fat per 100mL of a beverage. 

- Aim for less than 0.75g of saturated fat per 100mL of a beverage. 

- Aim for less than 0.2g of trans-fat per 100mL of a beverage. 

- ���������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������� ������������������������������� 

- The serving size on nutrition labels is usually for adults and is based on a 2000 calorie diet. The ������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������������ depending on your child’s age.
